2x" width="20"/>\n     </a>\n    </div>\n   </div>\n   <h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">\n    Hurricane Andrew\n   </h1>\n   <div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">\n    <div class="noprint" id="siteSub">\n     From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia\n    </div>\n    <div id="contentSub">\n    </div>\n    <div class="mw-jump" id="jump-to-nav">\n     Jump to:\n     <a </small>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <th scope="row" style="padding:0px 2px;white-space:nowrap">\n         Areas affected\n        </th>\n        <td style="padding:0px 2px">\n         <a href="/wiki/The_Bahamas" title="The Bahamas">\n          The Bahamas\n         </a>\n         ;\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/South_Florida_metropolitan_area" title="South Florida metropolitan area">\n          South Florida\n         </a>\n         ,\n         <a href="/wiki/Louisiana" title="Louisiana">\n          Louisiana\n         </a>\n         , and other areas of the\n         <a href="/wiki/Southern_United_States" title="Southern United States">\n          Southern United States\n         </a>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;padding:0px 2px">\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td colspan="2" style="text-align:center; border-top:#aaa 1px solid;">\n         Part of the\n         <b>\n          <a href="/wiki/1992_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="1992 Atlantic hurricane season">\n           1992 Atlantic hurricane season\n          </a>\n         </b>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr style="display:none">\n        <td colspan="2">\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;padding:0px 2px">\n         <p>\n          <span class="noprint">\n           <b>\n            History\n           </b>\n          </span>\n         </p>\n         <ul>\n          <li>\n           <span class="noprint">\n            <a href="/wiki/Meteorological_history_of_Hurricane_Andrew" title="Meteorological history of Hurricane Andrew">\n             Meteorological history\n            </a>\n           </span>\n          </li>\n         </ul>\n         <p>\n          <span class="noprint">\n           <b>\n            Effects\n           </b>\n          </span>\n         </p>\n         <ul>\n          <li>\n           <span class="noprint">\n            <small>\n             <a href="/wiki/Effects_of_Hurricane_Andrew_in_The_Bahamas" title="Effects of Hurricane Andrew in The Bahamas">\n              The Bahamas\n             </a>\n            </small>\n           </span>\n          </li>\n          <li>\n           <span class="noprint">\n            <small>\n             <a href="/wiki/Effects_of_Hurricane_Andrew_in_Florida" title="Effects of Hurricane Andrew in Florida">\n              Florida\n             </a>\n            </small>\n           </span>\n          </li>\n         </ul>\n         <p>\n          <span class="noprint">\n           <small>\n            <b>\n             Other wikis\n            </b>\n           </small>\n          </span>\n         </p>\n         <ul>\n          <li>\n           <span class="noprint">\n            <small>\n             <a class="extiw" href="https://commons.wikimedia.org/wiki/Category:Hurricane_Andrew" title="commons:Category:Hurricane Andrew">\n              commons:Category:Hurricane Andrew\n             </a>\n            </small>\n           </span>\n          </li>\n         </ul>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <p>\n       <b>\n        Hurricane Andrew\n       </b>\n       was a\n       <a href="/wiki/Saffir%E2%80%93Simpson_scale#Category_5" title="Saffir\xe2\x80\x93Simpson scale">\n        Category 5\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_hurricane" title="Atlantic hurricane">\n        Atlantic hurricane\n       </a>\n       that struck the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bahamas" title="Bahamas">\n        Bahamas\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Florida" title="Florida">\n        Florida\n       </a>\n       in mid-August 1992, the most destructive hurricane to ever hit the state. It was the strongest in decades and the\n       <a href="/wiki/List_of_costliest_Atlantic_hurricanes" title="List of costliest Atlantic hurricanes">\n        costliest hurricane\n       </a>\n       to make\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Landfall_(meteorology)" title="Landfall (meteorology)">\n        landfall\n       </a>\n       anywhere in the\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">\n        United States\n       </a>\n       until it was surpassed by\n       <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Katrina" title="Hurricane Katrina">\n        Katrina\n       </a>\n       in 2005. Andrew caused major damage in the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bahamas" title="Bahamas">\n        Bahamas\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Louisiana" title="Louisiana">\n        Louisiana\n       </a>\n       , but the greatest impact was felt in\n       <a href="/wiki/South_Florida" title="South Florida">\n        South Florida\n       </a>\n       , with sustained wind speeds as high as 165 mph (270 km/h). Passing directly through the city of\n       <a href="/wiki/Homestead,_Florida" title="Homestead, Florida">\n        Homestead\n       </a>\n       in\n       <a href="/wiki/Miami-Dade_County,_Florida" title="Miami-Dade County, Florida">\n        Dade County\n       </a>\n       (now known as Miami-Dade County), it stripped many homes of all but their concrete foundations. In total, it destroyed more than 63,500 houses, damaged more than 124,000 others, caused $26.5 billion in damage,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-1">\n         [nb 1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and left 65 people dead.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Andrew began as a\n       <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone#Tropical_depression" title="Tropical cyclone">\n        tropical depression\n       </a>\n       over the eastern Atlantic Ocean on August 16. After spending a week without significantly strengthening itself in the central Atlantic, it\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rapid_deepening" title="Rapid deepening">\n        rapidly intensified\n       </a>\n       into a powerful Category 5 hurricane while moving westward towards the Bahamas on August 23. Though it briefly weakened to Category 4 while traversing the Bahamas, it regained its Category 5 status before making landfall in Florida on\n       <a href="/wiki/Elliott_Key" title="Elliott Key">\n        Elliott Key\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Homestead,_Florida" title="Homestead, Florida">\n        Homestead\n       </a>\n       on August 24. With a barometric pressure of 922\n       <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">\n        mbar\n       </a>\n       (27.23\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Inches_of_mercury" title="Inches of mercury">\n        inHg\n       </a>\n       ) at the time of landfall in Florida, Andrew is the fourth most intense hurricane to strike the United States. Several hours later, the hurricane emerged over the\n       <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Mexico" title="Gulf of Mexico">\n        Gulf of Mexico\n       </a>\n       at Category 4 strength, with the\n       <a href="/wiki/Gulf_Coast_of_the_United_States" title="Gulf Coast of the United States">\n        Gulf Coast of the United States\n       </a>\n       in its path. After turning northwestward and weakening further, Andrew moved ashore near\n       <a href="/wiki/Morgan_City,_Louisiana" title="Morgan City, Louisiana">\n        Morgan City, Louisiana\n       </a>\n       , as a low-end Category 3 storm. After moving inland, the small hurricane curved northeastward and rapidly lost its intensity, merging with a\n       <a href="/wiki/Weather_front" title="Weather front">\n        frontal system\n       </a>\n       over the southern\n       <a href="/wiki/Appalachian_Mountains" title="Appalachian Mountains">\n        Appalachian Mountains\n       </a>\n       on August 28.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Hurricane Andrew first inflicted structural damage as it moved through the Bahamas, especially in\n       <a href="/wiki/Cat_Cays" title="Cat Cays">\n        Cat Cays\n       </a>\n       , lashing the islands with\n       <a href="/wiki/Storm_surge" title="Storm surge">\n        storm surge\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hurricane-force_winds" title="Hurricane-force winds">\n        hurricane-force winds\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Tornado" title="Tornado">\n        tornadoes\n       </a>\n       . About 800 houses were destroyed in the archipelago, and there was substantial damage to the transport, water, sanitation, agriculture, and fishing sectors. Andrew left four dead and $250 million in damage throughout the Bahamas. In parts of southern Florida, Andrew produced severe winds; a wind gust of 177 mph (282 km/h) was observed at a house in\n       <a href="/wiki/Perrine,_Florida" title="Perrine, Florida">\n        Perrine\n       </a>\n       . The cities of\n       <a href="/wiki/Florida_City,_Florida" title="Florida City, Florida">\n        Florida City\n       </a>\n       , Homestead, and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cutler_Ridge,_Florida" title="Cutler Ridge, Florida">\n        Cutler Ridge\n       </a>\n       received the brunt of the storm. As many as 1.4 million people lost power at the height of the storm. In the\n       <a href="/wiki/Everglades" title="Everglades">\n        Everglades\n       </a>\n       , 70,000 acres (280 km\n       <sup>\n        2\n       </sup>\n       ) of trees were downed, while invasive\n       <a href="/wiki/Burmese_python" title="Burmese python">\n        Burmese pythons\n       </a>\n       began\n       <a href="/wiki/Burmese_pythons_in_Florida" title="Burmese pythons in Florida">\n        inhabiting the region\n       </a>\n       after a nearby facility housing them was destroyed. Rainfall in Florida was substantial, peaking at 13.98 inches (355 mm) in western Dade County. In Florida, Andrew killed 44 and left a record $25 billion in damage.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Prior to making landfall in Louisiana on August 26, Andrew caused extensive damage to\n       <a href="/wiki/Offshore_oil_and_gas_in_the_Gulf_of_Mexico_(United_States)" title="Offshore oil and gas in the Gulf of Mexico (United States)">\n        oil platforms in the Gulf of Mexico\n       </a>\n       , leading to $500\xc2\xa0million in losses for oil companies. It produced hurricane-force winds along its path through Louisiana, damaging large stretches of power lines that left about 230,000 people without electricity. Over 80% of trees in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Atchafalaya_River" title="Atchafalaya River">\n        Atchafalaya River\n       </a>\n       basin were downed, and the agriculture there was devastated. Throughout the basin and\n       <a href="/wiki/Bayou_Lafourche" title="Bayou Lafourche">\n        Bayou Lafourche\n       </a>\n       , 187 million freshwater fish were killed in the hurricane. With 23,000 houses damaged, 985 others destroyed, and 1,951 mobile homes demolished, property losses in Louisiana exceeded $1.5 billion. The hurricane caused the deaths of 17\xc2\xa0people in the state, 6 of whom drowned offshore. Andrew spawned at least 28 tornadoes along the Gulf Coast, especially in\n       <a href="/wiki/Alabama" title="Alabama">\n        Alabama\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Georgia_(U.S._state)" title="Georgia (U.S. state)">\n        Georgia\n       </a>\n       , and Mississippi. In total, Andrew left 65 dead and caused $26.5\xc2\xa0billion in damage. It is currently the fifth costliest Atlantic hurricane to hit the United States, behind only Katrina,\n       <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Sandy" title="Hurricane Sandy">\n        Sandy\n       </a>\n       (2012),\n       <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Ike" title="Hurricane Ike">\n        Ike\n       </a>\n       (2008), and\n       <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Harvey" title="Hurricane Harvey">\n        Harvey\n       </a>\n       (2017), as well as the sixth costliest Atlantic hurricane, behind the aforementioned systems and\n       <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Wilma" title="Hurricane Wilma">\n        Wilma\n       </a>\n       (2005).\n      </p>\n      <p>\n      </p>\n      <div class="toc" id="toc">\n       <div class="toctitle">\n        <h2>\n         Contents\n        </h2>\n       </div>\n       <ul>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-1">\n         <a href="#Meteorological_history">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           1\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Meteorological history\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-2">\n         <a href="#Preparations">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           2\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Preparations\n          </span>\n         </a>\n         <ul>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-3">\n           <a href="#Bahamas">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             2.1\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Bahamas\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-4">\n           <a href="#Florida">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             2.2\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Florida\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-5">\n           <a href="#Gulf_Coast_of_the_United_States">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             2.3\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Gulf Coast of the United States\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n         </ul>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-6">\n         <a href="#Impact">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           3\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Impact\n          </span>\n         </a>\n         <ul>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-7">\n           <a href="#Bahamas_2">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             3.1\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Bahamas\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-8">\n           <a href="#Florida_2">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             3.2\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Florida\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-9">\n           <a href="#Louisiana">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             3.3\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Louisiana\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-10">\n           <a href="#Remainder_of_the_United_States">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             3.4\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Remainder of the United States\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n         </ul>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-11">\n         <a href="#Aftermath">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           4\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Aftermath\n          </span>\n         </a>\n         <ul>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-12">\n           <a href="#Bahamas_3">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             4.1\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Bahamas\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-13">\n           <a href="#United_States">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             4.2\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             United States\n            </span>\n           </a>\n           <ul>\n            <li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-14">\n             <a href="#Florida_3">\n              <span class="tocnumber">\n               4.2.1\n              </span>\n              <span class="toctext">\n               Florida\n              </span>\n             </a>\n            </li>\n            <li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-15">\n             <a href="#Louisiana_2">\n              <span class="tocnumber">\n               4.2.2\n              </span>\n              <span class="toctext">\n               Louisiana\n              </span>\n             </a>\n            </li>\n           </ul>\n          </li>\n         </ul>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-16">\n         <a href="#See_also">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           5\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           See also\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-17">\n         <a href="#Notes">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           6\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Notes\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-18">\n         <a href="#References">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           7\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           References\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-19">\n         <a href="#External_links">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           8\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           External links\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n       </ul>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Meteorological_history">\n        Meteorological history\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Andrew&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Meteorological history">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Meteorological_history_of_Hurricane_Andrew" title="Meteorological history of Hurricane Andrew">\n        Meteorological history of Hurricane Andrew\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Andrew_1992_track.png">\n         <img alt="The path of Hurricane Andrew, which starts in the open Atlantic Ocean and tracks northwestward. It curves westward while between Puerto Rico and Bermuda, eventually crossing the Bahamas and Florida. In the Gulf of Mexico, the track re-curves into Louisiana and stops over eastern Tennessee." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="633" data-file-width="1024" height="136" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Andrew_1992_track.png/220px-Andrew_1992_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Andrew_1992_track.png/330px-Andrew_1992_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Andrew_1992_track.png/440px-Andrew_1992_track.png 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Andrew_1992_track.png" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Map plotting the track and intensity of the storm, according to the\n         <a href="/wiki/Saffir%E2%80%93Simpson_scale" title="Saffir\xe2\x80\x93Simpson scale">\n          Saffir\xe2\x80\x93Simpson scale\n         </a>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       A\n       <a href="/wiki/Tropical_wave" title="Tropical wave">\n        tropical wave\n       </a>\n       moved off the west coast of Africa on August 14. A\n       <a href="/wiki/Ridge_(meteorology)" title="Ridge (meteorology)">\n        ridge\n       </a>\n       of high pressure to its north caused the wave to move quickly westward. An area of\n       <a href="/wiki/Convection" title="Convection">\n        convection\n       </a>\n       developed along the wave axis to the south of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Cape_Verde" title="Cape Verde">\n        Cape Verde\n       </a>\n       islands, and on August 15,\n       <a href="/wiki/Meteorology" title="Meteorology">\n        meteorologists\n       </a>\n       began classifying the system with the\n       <a href="/wiki/Dvorak_technique" title="Dvorak technique">\n        Dvorak technique\n       </a>\n       . The thunderstorm activity became more concentrated, and narrow spiral\n       <a href="/wiki/Rainband#Tropical_cyclones" title="Rainband">\n        rainbands\n       </a>\n       began to develop around a\n       <a href="/wiki/Atmospheric_circulation" title="Atmospheric circulation">\n        center of circulation\n       </a>\n       . It is estimated that Tropical Depression Three developed late on August 16, about 1,630\xc2\xa0mi (2,620\xc2\xa0km) east-southeast of\n       <a href="/wiki/Barbados" title="Barbados">\n        Barbados\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tcr_2-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-tcr-2">\n         [1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Embedded within the deep easterlies, the depression tracked west-northwestward at 20\xc2\xa0mph (32\xc2\xa0km/h).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-disc1_3-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-disc1-3">\n         [2]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Initially, moderate\n       <a href="/wiki/Wind_shear" title="Wind shear">\n        wind shear\n       </a>\n       prevented strengthening, until a decrease in shear allowed the depression to intensify into Tropical Storm Andrew at 12:00\n       <a href="/wiki/Coordinated_Universal_Time" title="Coordinated Universal Time">\n        UTC\n       </a>\n       on August 17.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tcr_2-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-tcr-2">\n         [1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       By early August 18, the storm maintained convection near the center with spiral bands to its west as the winds increased to 50\xc2\xa0mph (80\xc2\xa0km/h).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-disc5_4-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-disc5-4">\n         [3]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Shortly thereafter, the storm began weakening because of increased southwesterly wind shear from an upper-level low.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tcr_2-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-tcr-2">\n         [1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       On August 19, a\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hurricane_Hunters" title="Hurricane Hunters">\n        Hurricane Hunters\n       </a>\n       flight into the storm failed to locate a well-defined center\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-disc13_5-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-disc13-5">\n         [4]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and on the following day, a flight found that the cyclone had degenerated to the extent that only a diffuse low-level circulation center remained; observations indicated the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Barometric_pressure" title="Barometric pressure">\n        barometric pressure\n       </a>\n       rose to an unusually high 1,015\xc2\xa0mbar (29.97\xc2\xa0inHg). The flight indicated that Andrew maintained a vigorous circulation aloft. After the\n       <a href="/wiki/Cold-core_low" title="Cold-core low">\n        upper-level low\n       </a>\n       weakened and split into a\n       <a href="/wiki/Trough_(meteorology)" title="Trough (meteorology)">\n        trough\n       </a>\n       , the wind shear decreased over the storm. A strong high pressure cell then developed over the southeastern United States, which built eastward and caused Andrew to turn to the west.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tcr_2-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-tcr-2">\n         [1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Convection became more organized as upper-level\n       <a href="/wiki/Outflow_(meteorology)" title="Outflow (meteorology)">\n        outflow\n       </a>\n       became better established.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-disc20_6-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-disc20-6">\n         [5]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       An\n       <a href="/wiki/Eye_(cyclone)" title="Eye (cyclone)">\n        eye\n       </a>\n       formed, and Andrew attained hurricane status early on August 22, about 650\xc2\xa0mi (1,050\xc2\xa0km) east-southeast of\n       <a href="/wiki/Nassau,_Bahamas" title="Nassau, Bahamas">\n        Nassau, Bahamas\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tcr_2-4">\n        <a href="#cite_note-tcr-2">\n         [1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In the forecast issued six hours after becoming a hurricane, the cyclone was predicted to make\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Landfall_(meteorology)" title="Landfall (meteorology)">\n        landfall\n       </a>\n       near\n       <a href="/wiki/Jupiter,_Florida" title="Jupiter, Florida">\n        Jupiter, Florida\n       </a>\n       , with winds of 105 mph (170 km/h) on August 25.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-disc23_7-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-disc23-7">\n         [6]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       This underestimated both the strength and the speed of the storm, which would eventually make landfall in South Florida.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tcr_2-5">\n        <a href="#cite_note-tcr-2">\n         [1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:282px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hurricane_Andrew_sequence.jpg">\n         <img alt="A combination of three satellite views of Hurricane Andrew: approaching Florida, emerging into the Gulf of Mexico, and approaching Louisiana" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="512" data-file-width="768" height="187" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Hurricane_Andrew_sequence.jpg/280px-Hurricane_Andrew_sequence.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Hurricane_Andrew_sequence.jpg/420px-Hurricane_Andrew_sequence.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Hurricane_Andrew_sequence.jpg/560px-Hurricane_Andrew_sequence.jpg 2x" width="280"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hurricane_Andrew_sequence.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         A sequence of satellite images depicting Hurricane Andrew (from right to left) on August 23\xe2\x80\x9325\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The hurricane accelerated westward into an area of highly favorable conditions, and began to rapidly intensify late on August 22; in a 24\xe2\x80\x91hour period the atmospheric pressure dropped by 47\xc2\xa0mbar (1.388\xc2\xa0inHg) to a minimum of 922\xc2\xa0mbar (27.23\xc2\xa0inHg).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tcr_2-6">\n        <a href="#cite_note-tcr-2">\n         [1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       On August 23, the storm attained Category 5 status on the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saffir%E2%80%93Simpson_hurricane_scale" title="Saffir\xe2\x80\x93Simpson hurricane scale">\n        Saffir\xe2\x80\x93Simpson hurricane scale\n       </a>\n       , reaching\n       <a href="/wiki/Maximum_sustained_wind" title="Maximum sustained wind">\n        peak winds\n       </a>\n       of 175 mph (280 km/h) a short distance off\n       <a href="/wiki/Eleuthera" title="Eleuthera">\n        Eleuthera\n       </a>\n       island in the Bahamas at 18:00 UTC.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8">\n        <a href="#cite_note-8">\n         [nb 2]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-upgrade_9-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-upgrade-9">\n         [7]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Despite its intensity, Andrew was a small tropical cyclone, with winds of 35\xc2\xa0mph (56\xc2\xa0km/h) extending out only about 90 mi (150 km) from the center.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10">\n        <a href="#cite_note-10">\n         [8]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       After reaching that intensity, the hurricane underwent an\n       <a href="/wiki/Eye_(cyclone)#Eyewall_replacement_cycles" title="Eye (cyclone)">\n        eyewall replacement cycle\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-disc31_11-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-disc31-11">\n         [9]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       At 21:00 UTC on August 23, Andrew made landfall on Eleuthera with winds of 160\xc2\xa0mph (260\xc2\xa0km/h).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-upgrade_9-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-upgrade-9">\n         [7]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The cyclone weakened further while crossing the\n       <a href="/wiki/Bahama_Banks" title="Bahama Banks">\n        Bahama Banks\n       </a>\n       , and at 01:00 UTC on August 24, Andrew hit the southern\n       <a href="/wiki/Berry_Islands" title="Berry Islands">\n        Berry Islands\n       </a>\n       of the Bahamas with winds of 150\xc2\xa0mph (240\xc2\xa0km/h).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-upgrade_9-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-upgrade-9">\n         [7]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       As it crossed over the warm waters of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Gulf_Stream" title="Gulf Stream">\n        Gulf Stream\n       </a>\n       , the hurricane rapidly re-intensified as the eye decreased in size and its eyewall convection deepened.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tcr_2-7">\n        <a href="#cite_note-tcr-2">\n         [1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       At 08:40 UTC on August 24, Andrew struck\n       <a href="/wiki/Elliott_Key" title="Elliott Key">\n        Elliott Key\n       </a>\n       with winds of 165\xc2\xa0mph (266\xc2\xa0km/h) and a pressure of 926\xc2\xa0mbar (27.34\xc2\xa0inHg). About 25\xc2\xa0minutes after its first Florida landfall, Andrew hit just northeast of Homestead with a slightly lower pressure of 922\xc2\xa0mbar (27.23\xc2\xa0inHg).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-upgrade_9-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-upgrade-9">\n         [7]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       This barometric pressure made Andrew the most intense hurricane to strike the United States since\n       <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Camille" title="Hurricane Camille">\n        Hurricane Camille\n       </a>\n       in\n       <a href="/wiki/1969_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="1969 Atlantic hurricane season">\n        1969\n       </a>\n       and the strongest tropical cyclone to make landfall in Florida since the\n       <a href="/wiki/1935_Labor_Day_hurricane" title="1935 Labor Day hurricane">\n        Labor Day hurricane\n       </a>\n       of\n       <a href="/wiki/1935_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="1935 Atlantic hurricane season">\n        1935\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tcr_2-8">\n        <a href="#cite_note-tcr-2">\n         [1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <table class="wikitable" style="float: left; clear: left; margin: 0 1em 0.5em 0;">\n       <caption>\n        <b>\n         Most intense landfalling hurricanes in the\n         <a href="/wiki/Contiguous_United_States" title="Contiguous United States">\n          Contiguous United States\n         </a>\n        </b>\n        <br/>\n        <small>\n         Intensity is measured solely by central pressure\n        </small>\n       </caption>\n       <tr>\n        <th>\n         Rank\n        </th>\n        <th>\n         Hurricane\n        </th>\n        <th>\n         Season\n        </th>\n        <th>\n  </a>\n        </td>\n        <td align="center">\n         892\n         <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">\n          mbar\n         </a>\n         (\n         <a       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <th>\n         5\n        </th>\n        <td>\n         <a href="/wiki/1886_Indianola_hurricane" title="1886 Indianola hurricane">\n          "Indianola"\n         </a>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         <a href="/wiki/1886_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="1886 Atlantic hurricane season">\n          1886\n         </a>\n        </td>\n        <td season">\n          1919\n         </a>\n        </td>\n        <td align="center">\n         927 mbar (hPa)\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <th rowspan="2">\n         7\n        </th>\n        <td>\n         <a href="/wiki/1928_Okeechobee_hurricane" title="1928 Okeechobee hurricane">\n          "Okeechobee"\n         </a>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         <a href="/wiki/1928_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="1928 Atlantic hurricane season">\n          1928\n         </a>\n        </td>\n        <td align="center">\n         929 mbar (hPa)\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Irma" title="Hurricane Irma">\n          Irma\n         </a>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         <a       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <th rowspan="2">\n         9\n        </th>\n        <td>\n         <a href="/wiki/1926_Miami_hurricane" title="1926 Miami hurricane">\n          "Great Miami"\n         </a>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         <a href="/wiki/1926_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="1926 Atlantic hurricane season">\n          1926\n         </a>\n        </td>\n        <td align="center">\n         930 mbar (hPa)\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Donna" title="Hurricane Donna">\n          Donna\n         </a>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         <a href="/wiki/1960_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="1960 Atlantic hurricane season">\n          1960\n         </a>\n        </td>\n        <td align="center">\n         930 mbar (hPa)\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <th colspan="4">\n         <small>\n          Source: HURDAT,\n          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HURDAT_12-0">\n           <a href="#cite_note-HURDAT-12">\n            [10]\n           </a>\n          </sup>\n          Hurricane\n          <br/>\n          Research Division\n          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-US_hurricanes_13-0">\n           <a href="#cite_note-US_hurricanes-13">\n            [11]\n           </a>\n          </sup>\n         </small>\n        </th>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <p>\n       As the eye moved onshore in Florida, the convection in the eyewall strengthened due to increased convergence, and Hurricane Hunters reported a warmer eyewall temperature than two hours prior. However, Andrew weakened as it continued further inland, and after crossing southern Florida in four hours, the storm emerged into the Gulf of Mexico with winds of 130 mph (210 km/h).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tcr_2-9">\n        <a href="#cite_note-tcr-2">\n         [1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In the Gulf of Mexico, the eye remained well-defined as the hurricane turned to the west-northwest, a change due to the weakening of the ridge to its north.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-disc35_14-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-disc35-14">\n         [12]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Andrew steadily re-intensified over the Gulf of Mexico, reaching winds of 145 mph (235 km/h) late on August 25.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-upgrade_9-4">\n        <a href="#cite_note-upgrade-9">\n         [7]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       As the high pressure system to its north weakened, a strong mid-latitude trough approached the area from the northwest. This caused the hurricane to decelerate to the northwest, and winds decreased as Andrew approached the\n       <a href="/wiki/Gulf_Coast_of_the_United_States" title="Gulf Coast of the United States">\n        Gulf Coast of the United States\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tcr_2-10">\n        <a href="#cite_note-tcr-2">\n         [1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       At 08:30 UTC on August 26, the cyclone made landfall about 20 mi (30 km) west-southwest of Morgan City, Louisiana, with winds of 115\xc2\xa0mph (185\xc2\xa0km/h).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-upgrade_9-5">\n        <a href="#cite_note-upgrade-9">\n         [7]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Andrew weakened rapidly as it turned to the north and northeast, falling to tropical storm intensity within 10 hours. After entering Mississippi, the cyclone deteriorated to tropical depression status early on August 27. Accelerating northeastward, the depression began merging with the approaching frontal system, and by midday on August 28, Andrew merged with a\n       <a href="/wiki/Weather_front" title="Weather front">\n        frontal system\n       </a>\n       while located over the southern Appalachian Mountains.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tcr_2-11">\n        <a href="#cite_note-tcr-2">\n         [1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The remnants continued moving towards the northeast, and it lost its identity later that day, merging with the remnants of\n       <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Lester_(1992)" title="Hurricane Lester (1992)">\n        Hurricane Lester\n       </a>\n       and a frontal zone over the\n       <a href="/wiki/Mid-Atlantic_states" title="Mid-Atlantic states">\n        Mid-Atlantic\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rain_15-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-rain-15">\n         [13]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Post-analysis on Andrew revealed that the storm was often stronger than operationally reported between early on August 22 and early on August 26. In real time, the\n       <a href="/wiki/National_Hurricane_Center" title="National Hurricane Center">\n        National Hurricane Center\n       </a>\n       assessed its peak intensity as 150\xc2\xa0mph (240\xc2\xa0km/h),\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-disc30_16-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-disc30-16">\n         [14]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       which was upgraded to 155 mph (250 km/h) in a post-storm analysis after the season ended.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tcr_2-12">\n        <a href="#cite_note-tcr-2">\n         [1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       However, a 2004 paper by\n       <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Landsea" title="Christopher Landsea">\n        Christopher Landsea\n       </a>\n       and others concluded that Andrew became a Category 5 hurricane near the Bahamas on August 23 and reached maximum sustained winds of 175 mph (280 km/h). The paper also indicated that Andrew briefly re-intensified into a Category 5 hurricane around the time of landfall in South Florida early on August 24. The storm was found to have been slightly stronger while approaching Louisiana, but the landfall winds were decreased from 120 mph (195 km/h) to 115 mph (185 km/h).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-upgrade_9-6">\n        <a href="#cite_note-upgrade-9">\n         [7]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Preparations">\n        Preparations\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Andrew&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Preparations">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Andrew-Floyd.jpg">\n         <img alt="A comparison of two hurricanes, with the one of the left, Floyd, noticeably larger than the other, Andrew" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="386" data-file-width="800" height="106" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Andrew-Floyd.jpg/220px-Andrew-Floyd.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Andrew-Floyd.jpg/330px-Andrew-Floyd.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Andrew-Floyd.jpg/440px-Andrew-Floyd.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Andrew-Floyd.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Visual comparison of\n         <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Floyd" title="Hurricane Floyd">\n          Hurricane Floyd\n         </a>\n         and Hurricane Andrew while at similar positions and nearly identical intensities\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Bahamas">\n        Bahamas\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Andrew&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Bahamas">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Effects_of_Hurricane_Andrew_in_The_Bahamas" title="Effects of Hurricane Andrew in The Bahamas">\n        Effects of Hurricane Andrew in The Bahamas\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_the_Bahamas" title="Prime Minister of the Bahamas">\n        Bahamas Prime Minister\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Hubert_Ingraham" title="Hubert Ingraham">\n        Hubert Ingraham\n       </a>\n       , who took office while the storm was active, urged residents to "take this hurricane seriously".\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sutton_17-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-sutton-17">\n         [15]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Before the hurricane passed through the Bahamas, forecasters predicted a\n       <a href="/wiki/Storm_surge" title="Storm surge">\n        storm surge\n       </a>\n       of up to 18\xc2\xa0ft (5.5\xc2\xa0m), as well as up to 8\xc2\xa0in (200\xc2\xa0mm) of rain.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nhc30_18-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-nhc30-18">\n         [16]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       On August 22,\n       <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone_warnings_and_watches" title="Tropical cyclone warnings and watches">\n        hurricane watches\n       </a>\n       were issued from\n       <a href="/wiki/Andros,_Bahamas" title="Andros, Bahamas">\n        Andros\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Eleuthera" title="Eleuthera">\n        Eleuthera\n       </a>\n       islands northward through\n       <a href="/wiki/Grand_Bahama" title="Grand Bahama">\n        Grand Bahama\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Andros,_Bahamas" title="Andros, Bahamas">\n        Great Abaco\n       </a>\n       . They were upgraded to hurricane warnings later that day, and on August 23, additional warnings were issued for the central Bahamas, including\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cat_Island_(Bahamas)" title="Cat Island (Bahamas)">\n        Cat Island\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Exuma" title="Exuma">\n        Exuma\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/San_Salvador_Island" title="San Salvador Island">\n        San Salvador Island\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Long_Island,_Bahamas" title="Long Island, Bahamas">\n        Long Island\n       </a>\n       . All watches and warnings were discontinued on August 24.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tcr_2-13">\n        <a href="#cite_note-tcr-2">\n         [1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Advance warning was credited for the low death toll in the country.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wp_19-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-wp-19">\n         [17]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       A total of 58\xc2\xa0shelters were opened at churches, government buildings, and schools.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sutton_17-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-sutton-17">\n         [15]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Florida">\n        Florida\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Andrew&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Florida">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Effects_of_Hurricane_Andrew_in_Florida" title="Effects of Hurricane Andrew in Florida">\n        Effects of Hurricane Andrew in Florida\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:HurricaneAndrew.jpg">\n         <img alt="Infrared satellite image of Andrew, with its eye clearly visible" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="828" data-file-width="1024" height="178" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/HurricaneAndrew.jpg/220px-HurricaneAndrew.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/HurricaneAndrew.jpg/330px-HurricaneAndrew.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/HurricaneAndrew.jpg/440px-HurricaneAndrew.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:HurricaneAndrew.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Hurricane Andrew shortly after landfall near Homestead\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Initially, forecasters predicted tides up to 14\xc2\xa0ft (4.3\xc2\xa0m) above normal along the east coast of Florida, near the potential location of landfall.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20">\n        <a href="#cite_note-20">\n         [18]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Rainfall was projected to be between 5 and 8\xc2\xa0in (130 and 200\xc2\xa0mm) along the path of the storm. In addition, the National Hurricane Center noted the likelihood of isolated tornadoes in Central and South Florida during the passage of Andrew on August 23 and August 24.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">\n        <a href="#cite_note-21">\n         [19]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Several tropical storm and hurricane warnings were issued for much of Central and South Florida, from\n       <a href="/wiki/Titusville,_Florida" title="Titusville, Florida">\n        Titusville\n       </a>\n       on the east coast to\n       <a href="/wiki/Venice,_Florida" title="Venice, Florida">\n        Venice\n       </a>\n       on the west coast. Included in the warnings were\n       <a href="/wiki/Lake_Okeechobee" title="Lake Okeechobee">\n        Lake Okeechobee\n       </a>\n       and all of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Florida_Keys" title="Florida Keys">\n        Florida Keys\n       </a>\n       . By 18:00 UTC on August 24, all watches and warnings issued were discontinued after Andrew progressed into the Gulf of Mexico.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tcr_2-14">\n        <a href="#cite_note-tcr-2">\n         [1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Governor_of_Florida" title="Governor of Florida">\n        Governor\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Lawton_Chiles" title="Lawton Chiles">\n        Lawton Chiles\n       </a>\n       declared a\n       <a href="/wiki/State_of_emergency" title="State of emergency">\n        state of emergency\n       </a>\n       and activated about one-third of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Florida_National_Guard" title="Florida National Guard">\n        Florida National Guard\n       </a>\n       . Many residents evacuated, most voluntarily, from\n       <a href="/wiki/Broward_County,_Florida" title="Broward County, Florida">\n        Broward\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Charlotte_County,_Florida" title="Charlotte County, Florida">\n        Charlotte\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Collier_County,_Florida" title="Collier County, Florida">\n        Collier\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Lee_County,_Florida" title="Lee County, Florida">\n        Lee\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Martin_County,_Florida" title="Martin County, Florida">\n        Martin\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Miami-Dade_County,_Florida" title="Miami-Dade County, Florida">\n        Dade\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Monroe_County,_Florida" title="Monroe County, Florida">\n        Monroe\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Palm_Beach_County,_Florida" title="Palm Beach County, Florida">\n        Palm Beach\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Sarasota_County,_Florida" title="Sarasota County, Florida">\n        Sarasota\n       </a>\n       counties. A total of 142\xc2\xa0shelters opened in these counties and collectively housed at least 84,340\xc2\xa0people.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">\n        <a href="#cite_note-22">\n         [20]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In Dade County alone, 515,670\xc2\xa0people were ordered to evacuate.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23">\n        <a href="#cite_note-23">\n         [21]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       As Andrew was approaching, an estimated 20,000\xe2\x80\x9330,000\xc2\xa0tourists were in the Florida Keys (Monroe County).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-psheyw_24-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-psheyw-24">\n         [22]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Overall, almost 1.2\xc2\xa0million people evacuated, which contributed to the low number of fatalities, despite the intensity of the storm.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tcr_2-15">\n        <a href="#cite_note-tcr-2">\n         [1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Many evacuees also checked into hotels, with rooms completely booked as far north as\n       <a href="/wiki/Ocala,_Florida" title="Ocala, Florida">\n        Ocala\n       </a>\n       . Ultimately, the sheer number of evacuees led to likely the largest traffic jam in the history of Florida, mostly along\n       <a href="/wiki/Interstate_95_in_Florida" title="Interstate 95 in Florida">\n        Interstate 95\n       </a>\n       .\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Coast_Guard" title="United States Coast Guard">\n        United States Coast Guard\n       </a>\n       vessels on or near the Florida coastline were either secured onshore or sent to ride out the storm at sea.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25">\n        <a href="#cite_note-25">\n         [23]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Government offices and public and private schools were closed from Monroe County northward to\n       <a href="/wiki/St._Lucie_County,_Florida" title="St. Lucie County, Florida">\n        St. Lucie County\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26">\n        <a href="#cite_note-26">\n         [24]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Many colleges and universities in southeast Florida also closed, including\n       <a href="/wiki/Barry_University" title="Barry University">\n        Barry University\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Broward_Community_College" title="Broward Community College">\n        Broward Community College\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Florida_Atlantic_University" title="Florida Atlantic University">\n        Florida Atlantic University\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Florida_International_University" title="Florida International University">\n        Florida International University\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Nova_Southeastern_University" title="Nova Southeastern University">\n        Nova Southeastern University\n       </a>\n       , and the\n       <a href="/wiki/University_of_Miami" title="University of Miami">\n        University of Miami\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-miketyson_27-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-miketyson-27">\n         [25]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Major airports such as the\n       <a href="/wiki/Fort_Lauderdale%E2%80%93Hollywood_International_Airport" title="Fort Lauderdale\xe2\x80\x93Hollywood International Airport">\n        Fort Lauderdale\xe2\x80\x93Hollywood\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-miketyson_27-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-miketyson-27">\n         [25]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/Key_West_International_Airport" title="Key West International Airport">\n        Key West\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mh0827p1_28-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-mh0827p1-28">\n         [26]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/Miami_International_Airport" title="Miami International Airport">\n        Miami\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sutton_17-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-sutton-17">\n         [15]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Palm_Beach_International_Airport" title="Palm Beach International Airport">\n        Palm Beach\n       </a>\n       international airports closed.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-miketyson_27-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-miketyson-27">\n         [25]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Gulf_Coast_of_the_United_States">\n        Gulf Coast of the United States\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Andrew&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Gulf Coast of the United States">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hurricaneandrewlouisiana.JPG">\n         <img alt="A satellite imagery showing a hurricane approaching Louisiana" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="834" height="158" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Hurricaneandrewlouisiana.JPG/220px-Hurricaneandrewlouisiana.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Hurricaneandrewlouisiana.JPG/330px-Hurricaneandrewlouisiana.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Hurricaneandrewlouisiana.JPG/440px-Hurricaneandrewlouisiana.JPG 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hurricaneandrewlouisiana.JPG" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Satellite image of Hurricane Andrew approaching Louisiana\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Shortly after the storm emerged into the Gulf of Mexico from southern Florida, the National Hurricane Center issued hurricane watches and warnings for the Gulf Coast of the United States beginning at 13:00 UTC on August 24. After the initial hurricane watch from\n       <a href="/wiki/Mobile,_Alabama" title="Mobile, Alabama">\n        Mobile, Alabama\n       </a>\n       to\n       <a href="/wiki/Sabine_Pass,_Port_Arthur,_Texas" title="Sabine Pass, Port Arthur, Texas">\n        Sabine Pass, Texas\n       </a>\n       , the watches and warnings were expanded to eventually include areas from Mobile, Alabama, to\n       <a href="/wiki/Freeport,_Texas" title="Freeport, Texas">\n        Freeport, Texas\n       </a>\n       . All watches and warnings on the Gulf Coast were discontinued late on August 26 after the hurricane moved inland over Louisiana.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tcr_2-16">\n        <a href="#cite_note-tcr-2">\n         [1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Due to the hurricane\'s threat, workers fled oil platforms in the Gulf of Mexico, while the\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Coast_Guard" title="United States Coast Guard">\n        Coast Guard\n       </a>\n       moved their boats inland.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-frantz1_29-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-frantz1-29">\n         [27]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Officials in\n       <a href="/wiki/Mississippi" title="Mississippi">\n        Mississippi\n       </a>\n       suggested that about 100,000\xc2\xa0people evacuate the\n       <a href="/wiki/List_of_counties_in_Mississippi" title="List of counties in Mississippi">\n        coastal counties\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-frantz2_30-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-frantz2-30">\n         [28]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Shelters were opened in\n       <a href="/wiki/Hancock_County,_Mississippi" title="Hancock County, Mississippi">\n        Hancock\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Harrison_County,_Mississippi" title="Harrison County, Mississippi">\n        Harrison\n       </a>\n       counties, though only 68\xc2\xa0people went to a shelter in the former.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-al_31-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-al-31">\n         [29]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/Riverboat_casino" title="Riverboat casino">\n        Gambling ships\n       </a>\n       were moved into harbors and inland canals. Two run-offs for special\n       <a href="/wiki/Mississippi_Legislature" title="Mississippi Legislature">\n        legislative\n       </a>\n       elections scheduled for August 25 were postponed.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-frantz2_30-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-frantz2-30">\n         [28]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In\n       <a href="/wiki/Louisiana" title="Louisiana">\n        Louisiana\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Governor_of_Louisiana" title="Governor of Louisiana">\n        Governor\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Edwin_Edwards" title="Edwin Edwards">\n        Edwin Edwards\n       </a>\n       declared a state of emergency.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-frantz1_29-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-frantz1-29">\n         [27]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       About 1.25\xc2\xa0million people evacuated from the central and southeast Louisiana,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tcr_2-17">\n        <a href="#cite_note-tcr-2">\n         [1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       while approximately 60,000\xc2\xa0others fled\n       <a href="/wiki/List_of_parishes_in_Louisiana" title="List of parishes in Louisiana">\n        parishes\n       </a>\n       in southwest Louisiana.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32">\n        <a href="#cite_note-32">\n         [30]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       A mandatory evacuation from\n       <a href="/wiki/Grand_Isle,_Louisiana" title="Grand Isle, Louisiana">\n        Grand Isle\n       </a>\n       was ordered by Mayor Andy Valence and the city council.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33">\n        <a href="#cite_note-33">\n         [31]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In\n       <a href="/wiki/New_Orleans" title="New Orleans">\n        New Orleans\n       </a>\n       , Mayor\n       <a href="/wiki/Sidney_Barthelemy" title="Sidney Barthelemy">\n        Sidney Barthelemy\n       </a>\n       ordered the evacuation of about 200,000\xc2\xa0residents in the low-lying areas of the city.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-standard_34-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-standard-34">\n         [32]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Nine shelters were opened in the city, which were occupied by thousands of people.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-frantz2_30-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-frantz2-30">\n         [28]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In response to computer simulations showing that storm surge from a tropical cyclone like Hurricane Andrew could over-top\n       <a href="/wiki/Drainage_in_New_Orleans" title="Drainage in New Orleans">\n        the levees\n       </a>\n       , workers closed 111\n       <a href="/wiki/Floodgate" title="Floodgate">\n        floodgates\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-standard_34-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-standard-34">\n         [32]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Louis_Armstrong_New_Orleans_International_Airport" title="Louis Armstrong New Orleans International Airport">\n        Louis Armstrong New Orleans International Airport\n       </a>\n       closed, with jumbo jets being flown to other airports. A total of 250\xc2\xa0members of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Louisiana_National_Guard" title="Louisiana National Guard">\n        Louisiana National Guard\n       </a>\n       patrolled the streets during the storm. The\n       <a href="/wiki/American_Red_Cross" title="American Red Cross">\n        Red Cross\n       </a>\n       assisted with opening a shelter at the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/University_of_Southwest_Louisiana" title="University of Southwest Louisiana">\n        University of Southwest Louisiana\n       </a>\n       \'s\n       <a href="/wiki/Cajundome" title="Cajundome">\n        Cajundome\n       </a>\n       in\n       <a href="/wiki/Lafayette,_Louisiana" title="Lafayette, Louisiana">\n        Lafayette\n       </a>\n       , equipped to handle about 2,000\xc2\xa0people.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-frantz2_30-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-frantz2-30">\n         [28]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In\n       <a href="/wiki/Texas" title="Texas">\n        Texas\n       </a>\n       , about 250,000\xc2\xa0people evacuated\n       <a href="/wiki/Orange_County,_Texas" title="Orange County, Texas">\n        Orange\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Jefferson_County,_Texas" title="Jefferson County, Texas">\n        Jefferson\n       </a>\n       counties.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tcr_2-18">\n        <a href="#cite_note-tcr-2">\n         [1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/Galveston,_Texas" title="Galveston, Texas">\n        Galveston\n       </a>\n       City Manager Doug Matthews advised residents to develop an evacuation plan in the event that the city chose to call for evacuations.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nbhz_35-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-nbhz-35">\n         [33]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The city later decided against ordering an evacuation.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36">\n        <a href="#cite_note-36">\n         [34]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       School was canceled on August 25 for\n       <a href="/wiki/Beaumont,_Texas" title="Beaumont, Texas">\n        Beaumont\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Port_Arthur,_Texas" title="Port Arthur, Texas">\n        Port Arthur\n       </a>\n       , and other areas of central Jefferson County,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nbhz_35-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-nbhz-35">\n         [33]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       while schools were closed in\n       <a href="/wiki/Dickinson,_Texas" title="Dickinson, Texas">\n        Dickinson\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/High_Island,_Texas" title="High Island, Texas">\n        High Island\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Hitchcock,_Texas" title="Hitchcock, Texas">\n        Hitchcock\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/La_Marque,_Texas" title="La Marque, Texas">\n        La Marque\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Santa_Fe,_Texas" title="Santa Fe, Texas">\n        Santa Fe\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Texas_City,_Texas" title="Texas City, Texas">\n        Texas City\n       </a>\n       on August 26.\n       <a href="/wiki/College_of_the_Mainland" title="College of the Mainland">\n        College of the Mainland\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Galveston_College" title="Galveston College">\n        Galveston College\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Texas_A%26M_University_at_Galveston" title="Texas A&amp;M University at Galveston">\n        Texas A&amp;M University at Galveston\n       </a>\n       were also closed.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37">\n        <a href="#cite_note-37">\n         [35]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Emergency management crews in\n       <a href="/wiki/Corpus_Christi,_Texas" title="Corpus Christi, Texas">\n        Corpus Christi\n       </a>\n       began testing emergency generators and severe weather gear.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nbhz_35-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-nbhz-35">\n         [33]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Comal_County,_Texas" title="Comal County, Texas">\n        Comal County\n       </a>\n       chapter of the Red Cross placed their disaster alert teams on standby and ready to respond if the hurricane threatened the\n       <a href="/wiki/Corpus_Christi_metropolitan_area" title="Corpus Christi metropolitan area">\n        Corpus Christi area\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">\n        <a href="#cite_note-38">\n         [36]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Impact">\n        Impact\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Andrew&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Impact">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span $18.8\xc2\xa0billion\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <th>\n         8\n        </th>\n        <td>\n         <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Irene" title="Hurricane Irene">\n          Irene\n         </a>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         <a href="/wiki/2011_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="2011 Atlantic hurricane season">\n          2011\n         </a>\n        </td>\n   <th>\n         9\n        </th>\n        <td>\n         <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Charley" title="Hurricane Charley">\n          Charley\n         </a>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         <a id="cite_ref-Dead_2011_39-0">\n          <a href="#cite_note-Dead_2011-39">\n           [37]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40">\n          <a href="#cite_note-40">\n           [38]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41">\n          <a href="#cite_note-41">\n           [39]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42">\n          <a href="#cite_note-42">\n           [nb 3]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </th>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <p>\n       Though Andrew was a small tropical cyclone for most of its lifespan, it caused extreme damage, especially in the Bahamas, Florida, and Louisiana. The vast majority of the damage was as a result of extremely high winds, although a few tornadoes spawned by Andrew caused considerable damage in Louisiana. Throughout the areas affected, almost 177,000\xc2\xa0people were left homeless. Outside of the Bahamas, Florida, and Louisiana, effects were widespread, although damage was minimal. Overall, $26.5\xc2\xa0billion in losses and 65\xc2\xa0fatalities were attributed to Andrew,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tcr_2-19">\n        <a href="#cite_note-tcr-2">\n         [1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       with some estimates ranging as high as $34\xc2\xa0billion.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43">\n        <a href="#cite_note-43">\n         [40]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Andrew was the costliest hurricane in U.S. history at the time, but is now fifth following hurricanes\n       <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Katrina" title="Hurricane Katrina">\n        Katrina\n       </a>\n       (2005),\n       <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Sandy" title="Hurricane Sandy">\n        Sandy\n       </a>\n       (2012),\n       <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Harvey" title="Hurricane Harvey">\n        Harvey\n       </a>\n       (2017), and\n       <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Ike" title="Hurricane Ike">\n        Ike\n       </a>\n       (2008).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44">\n        <a href="#cite_note-44">\n         [41]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Bahamas_2">\n        Bahamas\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Andrew&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Bahamas">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Effects_of_Hurricane_Andrew_in_The_Bahamas" title="Effects of Hurricane Andrew in The Bahamas">\n        Effects of Hurricane Andrew in The Bahamas\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       In the Bahamas, Andrew produced hurricane-force winds in\n       <a href="/wiki/North_Eleuthera" title="North Eleuthera">\n        North Eleuthera\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/New_Providence" title="New Providence">\n        New Providence\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/North_Andros" title="North Andros">\n        North Andros\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Bimini" title="Bimini">\n        Bimini\n       </a>\n       , and the Berry Islands.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bah2_45-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-bah2-45">\n         [42]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The storm first struck North Eleuthera,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reanal_46-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-reanal-46">\n         [43]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       where it produced a high storm surge.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wp_19-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-wp-19">\n         [17]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       At a small village in the northwestern portion of the island, more than half of the houses were destroyed and the rest of the buildings sustained minor to major damage. One person drowned from the surge in Lower Bogue, Eleuthera, and two others died in\n       <a href="/wiki/The_Bluff,_Bahamas" title="The Bluff, Bahamas">\n        The Bluff\n       </a>\n       . On Current Island, the hurricane destroyed 24 of the 30 houses.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bah4_47-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-bah4-47">\n         [44]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/Harbour_Island,_Bahamas" title="Harbour Island, Bahamas">\n        Harbour Island\n       </a>\n       , near Eleuthera, reported wind gusts of 138\xc2\xa0mph (222\xc2\xa0km/h) \xe2\x80\x93 the strongest gust speed observed in the Bahamas during Andrew\'s passage.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tcr_2-20">\n        <a href="#cite_note-tcr-2">\n         [1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       News reports indicated severe damage to 36 houses on Harbor Island.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rw_48-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-rw-48">\n         [45]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Andrew produced several tornadoes in the area.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bah3_49-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-bah3-49">\n         [46]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       At the capital city of\n       <a href="/wiki/Nassau,_Bahamas" title="Nassau, Bahamas">\n        Nassau\n       </a>\n       , sustained winds reached 92\xc2\xa0mph (148\xc2\xa0km/h), while gusts up to 115\xc2\xa0mph (185\xc2\xa0km/h) were reported.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tcr_2-21">\n        <a href="#cite_note-tcr-2">\n         [1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Only minor damage occurred in Nassau, according to the Bahamas Red Cross,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rw_48-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-rw-48">\n         [45]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       but on the private island of Cat Cay, many expensive homes sustained heavy damage.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nyt_50-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-nyt-50">\n         [47]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Much of the northwestern Bahamas received damage,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bah3_49-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-bah3-49">\n         [46]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       with estimated monetary losses reaching $250\xc2\xa0million.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tcr_2-22">\n        <a href="#cite_note-tcr-2">\n         [1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       A total of 800 houses were destroyed, leaving 1,700 people homeless. Additionally, the storm caused severe damage to the sectors of transport, communications, water, sanitation, agriculture, and fishing.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rw_48-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-rw-48">\n         [45]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Four deaths in the country were attributed to the hurricane, of which three were direct;\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tcr_2-23">\n        <a href="#cite_note-tcr-2">\n         [1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       the indirect fatality was due to heart failure during the passage of the storm.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bah4_47-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-bah4-47">\n         [44]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52">\n        <a href="#cite_note-52">\n         [nb 4]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Florida_2">\n        Florida\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Andrew&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Florida">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Effects_of_Hurricane_Andrew_in_Florida" title="Effects of Hurricane Andrew in Florida">\n        Effects of Hurricane Andrew in Florida\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hurricane_andrew_fema_2563.jpg">\n         <img alt="A community with nearly every trailer flattened" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1952" data-file-width="2940" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Hurricane_andrew_fema_2563.jpg/220px-Hurricane_andrew_fema_2563.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Hurricane_andrew_fema_2563.jpg/330px-Hurricane_andrew_fema_2563.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Hurricane_andrew_fema_2563.jpg/440px-Hurricane_andrew_fema_2563.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hurricane_andrew_fema_2563.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Damage from Hurricane Andrew in a large mobile home community\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Overall, Andrew caused about $25.3\xc2\xa0billion in damage in Florida,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tcr_2-24">\n        <a href="#cite_note-tcr-2">\n         [1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       making it the costliest hurricane to hit the state.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-floridarecord_53-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-floridarecord-53">\n         [49]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Almost all of the damage in Florida was caused by strong winds.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tcr_2-25">\n        <a href="#cite_note-tcr-2">\n         [1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Of the 44\xc2\xa0deaths attributed to the storm, 15\xc2\xa0were direct fatalities, while 29\xc2\xa0were indirectly caused by the storm. It was later noted that if Andrew had been slightly larger or had made landfall a few miles further north, it would have significantly affected\n       <a href="/wiki/Miami" title="Miami">\n        Miami\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Fort_Lauderdale,_Florida" title="Fort Lauderdale, Florida">\n        Fort Lauderdale\n       </a>\n       , which would have resulted in an even higher damage and death toll.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tcr_2-26">\n        <a href="#cite_note-tcr-2">\n         [1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       An analysis by the\n       <a href="/wiki/American_Meteorological_Society" title="American Meteorological Society">\n        American Meteorological Society\n       </a>\n       indicated that unlike most hurricanes, wind damage from Andrew was mostly north of the geometric center and occurred primarily on the eastern edge of the storm.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54">\n        <a href="#cite_note-54">\n         [50]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Some officials in Florida considered Andrew the worst storm in the state since the\n       <a href="/wiki/1935_Labor_Day_hurricane" title="1935 Labor Day hurricane">\n        Labor Day hurricane in 1935\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mt2_55-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-mt2-55">\n         [51]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The storm surge from Andrew caused more than $500\xc2\xa0million in losses to boats and buildings.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tcr_2-27">\n        <a href="#cite_note-tcr-2">\n         [1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56">\n        <a href="#cite_note-56">\n         [52]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       At the height of the storm, more than 1.4\xc2\xa0million people lost electricity and another 150,000\xc2\xa0were without telephone service.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-facts_57-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-facts-57">\n         [53]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       It is estimated that throughout
