Florida, the storm damaged 101,241\xc2\xa0homes and destroyed approximately 63,000\xc2\xa0others \xe2\x80\x93 the vast majority in Dade County \xe2\x80\x93 with about 175,000\xc2\xa0people rendered homeless.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tcr_2-28">\n        <a href="#cite_note-tcr-2">\n         [1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58">\n        <a href="#cite_note-58">\n         [54]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In addition to homes, the storm damaged or destroyed 82,000\xc2\xa0businesses, 32,900\n       <a href="/wiki/Acre" title="Acre">\n        acres\n       </a>\n       (13,300\n       <a href="/wiki/Hectare" title="Hectare">\n        ha\n       </a>\n       ) of farmland, 31\xc2\xa0public schools, 59\xc2\xa0health facilities/hospitals, 9,500\xc2\xa0traffic signals, 3,300\xc2\xa0mi (5,300\xc2\xa0km) of power lines, and 3,000\xc2\xa0watermains.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-facts_57-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-facts-57">\n         [53]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Approximately 20\xc2\xa0million cubic yards (15\xc2\xa0million\n       <a href="/wiki/Cubic_metre" title="Cubic metre">\n        m\n        <sup>\n         3\n        </sup>\n       </a>\n       ) of debris left by the storm were disposed of.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59">\n        <a href="#cite_note-59">\n         [55]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Tides were generally between 4 to 6\xc2\xa0ft (1.2 to 1.8\xc2\xa0m) above normal in the Biscayne Bay area, though near the\n       <a href="/wiki/Burger_King" title="Burger King">\n        Burger King International Headquarters\n       </a>\n       , tides reached as high as 16.9\xc2\xa0ft (5.2\xc2\xa0m) above normal. Storm surge on the west coast was widespread but generally light, with a peak height of 6\xc2\xa0ft (1.8\xc2\xa0m) in\n       <a href="/wiki/Everglades_City,_Florida" title="Everglades City, Florida">\n        Everglades City\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Goodland,_Florida" title="Goodland, Florida">\n        Goodland\n       </a>\n       . Strong winds from the storm were confined to a relatively small area, stretching from\n       <a href="/wiki/Key_Largo" title="Key Largo">\n        Key Largo\n       </a>\n       to the\n       <a href="/wiki/Miami_Beach,_Florida" title="Miami Beach, Florida">\n        Miami Beach\n       </a>\n       area. A house near\n       <a href="/wiki/Perrine,_Florida" title="Perrine, Florida">\n        Perrine\n       </a>\n       initially reported a wind gust of 212\xc2\xa0mph (341\xc2\xa0km/h) before the structure and instrument were destroyed; this measurement was reduced to 177\xc2\xa0mph (285\xc2\xa0km/h), after wind-tunnel testing at the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Virginia_Polytechnic_Institute_and_State_University" title="Virginia Polytechnic Institute and State University">\n        Virginia Polytechnic Institute and State University\n       </a>\n       of the same type of anemometer revealed a 16.5% error. Several other anemometers measuring the highest wind speeds on land were destroyed or failed. At the National Hurricane Center building in\n       <a href="/wiki/Coral_Gables,_Florida" title="Coral Gables, Florida">\n        Coral Gables\n       </a>\n       , sustained winds of 115\xc2\xa0mph (185\xc2\xa0km/h) and gusts to 164\xc2\xa0mph (264\xc2\xa0km/h) were measured before the anemometer failed. The highest sustained wind speed for the storm was 146\xc2\xa0mph (235\xc2\xa0km/h), recorded at the\n       <a href="/wiki/Turkey_Point_Nuclear_Generating_Station" title="Turkey Point Nuclear Generating Station">\n        Turkey Point Nuclear Generating Station\n       </a>\n       , before instruments also failed there. In Key Largo, a 13-minute wind speed of 114\xc2\xa0mph (183\xc2\xa0km/h) was reported. Tropical storm force winds reached as far north as\n       <a href="/wiki/West_Palm_Beach,_Florida" title="West Palm Beach, Florida">\n        West Palm Beach\n       </a>\n       . On the west coast of Florida, sustained winds remained just below tropical storm force on\n       <a href="/wiki/Marco_Island,_Florida" title="Marco Island, Florida">\n        Marco Island\n       </a>\n       , though a wind gust of 100\xc2\xa0mph (160\xc2\xa0km/h) was reported in Collier County. Rainfall was generally light, possibly as a result of the storm\'s relatively fast movement.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tcr_2-29">\n        <a href="#cite_note-tcr-2">\n         [1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Overall, precipitation from Andrew peaked at nearly 14\xc2\xa0in (360\xc2\xa0mm) in western Dade County. Heavy rainfall in other areas was sporadic, with precipitation reported as far north as\n       <a href="/wiki/Central_Florida" title="Central Florida">\n        Central Florida\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rain_15-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-rain-15">\n         [13]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Destruction_following_hurricane_andrew.jpg">\n         <img alt="A close-up view of houses with evident wind damage" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1832" height="144" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Destruction_following_hurricane_andrew.jpg/220px-Destruction_following_hurricane_andrew.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Destruction_following_hurricane_andrew.jpg/330px-Destruction_following_hurricane_andrew.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Destruction_following_hurricane_andrew.jpg/440px-Destruction_following_hurricane_andrew.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Destruction_following_hurricane_andrew.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Damage in\n         <a href="/wiki/Lakes_by_the_Bay,_Florida" title="Lakes by the Bay, Florida">\n          Lakes by the Bay\n         </a>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Although effects from Andrew were catastrophic, the extent of damage was limited mainly from\n       <a href="/wiki/Kendall,_Florida" title="Kendall, Florida">\n        Kendall\n       </a>\n       to Key Largo due to the small wind field of the storm. The hurricane destroyed 90% of mobile homes in the county, including 99% of mobile homes in\n       <a href="/wiki/Homestead,_Florida" title="Homestead, Florida">\n        Homestead\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tcr_2-30">\n        <a href="#cite_note-tcr-2">\n         [1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       At the\n       <a href="/wiki/Homestead_Air_Reserve_Base" title="Homestead Air Reserve Base">\n        Homestead Air Force Base\n       </a>\n       , most of the 2,000\xc2\xa0buildings on the base were severely damaged or rendered unusable.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wp0825p1_60-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-wp0825p1-60">\n         [56]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Damage to the base was extensive enough that it was recommended for closure.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-homesteadafbclosing_61-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-homesteadafbclosing-61">\n         [57]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Nearby, in the small town of\n       <a href="/wiki/Florida_City,_Florida" title="Florida City, Florida">\n        Florida City\n       </a>\n       , over 120\xc2\xa0homes were demolished and 700\xc2\xa0others were damaged, while a number of other buildings were damaged beyond repair, including City Hall.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62">\n        <a href="#cite_note-62">\n         [58]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Further north, damage to poorly constructed homes in communities such as\n       <a href="/wiki/Country_Walk,_Florida" title="Country Walk, Florida">\n        Country Walk\n       </a>\n       and Saga Bay resembled that of an\n       <a href="/wiki/Fujita_scale" title="Fujita scale">\n        F3 tornado\n       </a>\n       , as winds in the area were estimated to have ranged from 130 to 150\xc2\xa0mph (210 to 240\xc2\xa0km/h), below the threshold for an F3 tornado.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63">\n        <a href="#cite_note-63">\n         [59]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Four of the five condominiums at Naranja Lakes were destroyed.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SPT_64-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-SPT-64">\n         [60]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Southland_Mall_(Miami)" title="Southland Mall (Miami)">\n        Cutler Ridge Mall\n       </a>\n       suffered severe wind and water damage; after the storm, significant looting was reported at that location.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65">\n        <a href="#cite_note-65">\n         [61]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       More than 50\xc2\xa0streets were blocked by fallen trees and power lines.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66">\n        <a href="#cite_note-66">\n         [62]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Agriculture suffered extensively as well, with an 85% loss to fruit crops such as avocados, limes, and mangoes. Crop damage in Dade County totaled about $509\xc2\xa0million.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67">\n        <a href="#cite_note-67">\n         [63]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The county suffered the vast majority of the damage from the hurricane, totaling approximately $25\xc2\xa0billion. Andrew left at least 40\xc2\xa0deaths in the county, 15\xc2\xa0direct and 25\xc2\xa0indirect.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tcr_2-31">\n        <a href="#cite_note-tcr-2">\n         [1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dadeland_Mobile_Home_Park_after_Andrew_-_Flickr_-_NOAA_Photo_Library.jpg">\n         <img alt="An aerial view of destroyed mobile homes with copious amounts of debris" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2352" data-file-width="3672" height="141" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Dadeland_Mobile_Home_Park_after_Andrew_-_Flickr_-_NOAA_Photo_Library.jpg/220px-Dadeland_Mobile_Home_Park_after_Andrew_-_Flickr_-_NOAA_Photo_Library.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Dadeland_Mobile_Home_Park_after_Andrew_-_Flickr_-_NOAA_Photo_Library.jpg/330px-Dadeland_Mobile_Home_Park_after_Andrew_-_Flickr_-_NOAA_Photo_Library.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Dadeland_Mobile_Home_Park_after_Andrew_-_Flickr_-_NOAA_Photo_Library.jpg/440px-Dadeland_Mobile_Home_Park_after_Andrew_-_Flickr_-_NOAA_Photo_Library.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Dadeland_Mobile_Home_Park_after_Andrew_-_Flickr_-_NOAA_Photo_Library.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         The Dadeland Mobile Home Park after Andrew\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Elsewhere, effects were relatively minimal, except in Broward, Monroe, and Collier counties. In Broward County, on the north side of the storm\'s path, impact in several municipalities was primarily limited to downed trees, several of which fell onto roads and power lines. In\n       <a href="/wiki/Pembroke_Park,_Florida" title="Pembroke Park, Florida">\n        Pembroke Park\n       </a>\n       , one of the worst impacted cities in the county, approximately 260\xc2\xa0mobile homes were damaged. Storm surge left coastal flooding in some areas, especially along state roads\n       <a href="/wiki/Florida_State_Road_A1A" title="Florida State Road A1A">\n        A1A\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Florida_State_Road_858" title="Florida State Road 858">\n        858\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68">\n        <a href="#cite_note-68">\n         [64]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Property damage reached about $100\xc2\xa0million and three fatalities were reported in Broward County.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tcr_2-32">\n        <a href="#cite_note-tcr-2">\n         [1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In\n       <a href="/wiki/Everglades_National_Park" title="Everglades National Park">\n        Everglades National Park\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Biscayne_National_Park" title="Biscayne National Park">\n        Biscayne National Park\n       </a>\n       , more than 25% of trees were damaged or destroyed, including one-fourth of the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Royal_palm" title="Royal palm">\n        royal palms\n       </a>\n       and one-third of the pine trees in the former.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69">\n        <a href="#cite_note-69">\n         [65]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In addition to the damage at Everglades National Park, effects in Monroe County were significant, especially in the Upper Florida Keys. Strong winds damaged billboards, awnings, commercial signs, several boats, planes, trees,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mh0827p1_28-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-mh0827p1-28">\n         [26]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and 1,500\xc2\xa0homes, with 300\xc2\xa0of those becoming uninhabitable.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-psheyw_24-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-psheyw-24">\n         [22]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Damage in that county was about $131\xc2\xa0million.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tcr_2-33">\n        <a href="#cite_note-tcr-2">\n         [1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In\n       <a href="/wiki/Collier_County,_Florida" title="Collier County, Florida">\n        Collier County\n       </a>\n       , to the north of the storm\'s path, sustained winds up to 98\xc2\xa0mph (158\xc2\xa0km/h) were observed in\n       <a href="/wiki/Chokoloskee,_Florida" title="Chokoloskee, Florida">\n        Chokoloskee\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70">\n        <a href="#cite_note-70">\n         [66]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Storm surge flooded low-lying areas, particularly in Goodland, Everglades City, and Marco Island. Many boats were damaged or destroyed by the rough seas and strong winds.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71">\n        <a href="#cite_note-71">\n         [67]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The storm destroyed 80\xc2\xa0mobile homes and severely damaged 400\xc2\xa0others.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72">\n        <a href="#cite_note-72">\n         [68]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Property damage in the county reached about $30\xc2\xa0million.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tcr_2-34">\n        <a href="#cite_note-tcr-2">\n         [1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Louisiana">\n        Louisiana\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Andrew&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Louisiana">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Andrewlaplacetornado.png">\n         <img alt="Significant tornado damage inflicted upon a home, with its exterior walls missing and some of its interior walls and roof destroyed" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="412" data-file-width="538" height="168" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Andrewlaplacetornado.png/220px-Andrewlaplacetornado.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Andrewlaplacetornado.png/330px-Andrewlaplacetornado.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Andrewlaplacetornado.png/440px-Andrewlaplacetornado.png 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Andrewlaplacetornado.png" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Damage from an F3 tornado spawned by Andrew in LaPlace\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       After hitting Florida, Andrew moved across the Gulf of Mexico and made landfall about 23\xc2\xa0mi (37\xc2\xa0km) west-southwest of Morgan City in south-central Louisiana; at landfall, the maximum sustained winds were 115\xc2\xa0mph (185\xc2\xa0km/h). The highest sustained wind speed observed was 96\xc2\xa0mph (154\xc2\xa0km/h), while a wind gust as strong as 120\xc2\xa0mph (190\xc2\xa0km/h) was recorded; both measurements were taken at the fire station in\n       <a href="/wiki/Berwick,_Louisiana" title="Berwick, Louisiana">\n        Berwick\n       </a>\n       . As it moved ashore, the hurricane produced storm tides of at least 8\xc2\xa0ft (2.4\xc2\xa0m) above normal, causing flooding along the coast from\n       <a href="/wiki/Vermilion_Bay_(Louisiana)" title="Vermilion Bay (Louisiana)">\n        Vermilion Bay\n       </a>\n       to\n       <a href="/wiki/Lake_Borgne" title="Lake Borgne">\n        Lake Borgne\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tcr_2-35">\n        <a href="#cite_note-tcr-2">\n         [1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Off Louisiana, a group of six fishermen from Alabama drowned.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-al_31-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-al-31">\n         [29]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Heavy rains accompanied the storm\'s passage through the state, peaking at 11.02\xc2\xa0in (280\xc2\xa0mm) in\n       <a href="/wiki/Robert,_Louisiana" title="Robert, Louisiana">\n        Robert\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tcr_2-36">\n        <a href="#cite_note-tcr-2">\n         [1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       River flooding was also reported, with the\n       <a href="/wiki/Tangipahoa_River" title="Tangipahoa River">\n        Tangipahoa River\n       </a>\n       in Robert cresting at 3.8\xc2\xa0ft (1.2\xc2\xa0m) above flood stage.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-new2_73-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-new2-73">\n         [69]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Before making landfall, Andrew spawned an\n       <a href="/wiki/Fujita_scale" title="Fujita scale">\n        F3\n       </a>\n       tornado in\n       <a href="/wiki/LaPlace,_Louisiana" title="LaPlace, Louisiana">\n        LaPlace\n       </a>\n       , which killed two people and injuring 32.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tcr_2-37">\n        <a href="#cite_note-tcr-2">\n         [1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-new2_73-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-new2-73">\n         [69]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The tornado was on the ground for about 10\xc2\xa0minutes, during which it damaged or destroyed 163\xc2\xa0structures, leaving 60\xc2\xa0families homeless.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-new2_73-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-new2-73">\n         [69]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Collectively, 14\xc2\xa0tornadoes were reported in the parishes of\n       <a href="/wiki/Ascension_Parish,_Louisiana" title="Ascension Parish, Louisiana">\n        Ascension\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Iberville_Parish,_Louisiana" title="Iberville Parish, Louisiana">\n        Iberville\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Pointe_Coupee_Parish,_Louisiana" title="Pointe Coupee Parish, Louisiana">\n        Pointe Coupee\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Avoyelles_Parish,_Louisiana" title="Avoyelles Parish, Louisiana">\n        Avoyelles\n       </a>\n       , as well as in\n       <a href="/wiki/Baton_Rouge,_Louisiana" title="Baton Rouge, Louisiana">\n        Baton Rouge\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tcr_2-38">\n        <a href="#cite_note-tcr-2">\n         [1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ncdc_74-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ncdc-74">\n         [70]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Along the Louisiana coastline, impact largely resembled that of a Category 2 hurricane. Damage was heaviest in\n       <a href="/wiki/St._Mary_Parish,_Louisiana" title="St. Mary Parish, Louisiana">\n        St. Mary Parish\n       </a>\n       , about 32\xc2\xa0mi (51\xc2\xa0km) east of where Andrew made landfall. Twenty-six schools were impacted, with damage totaling $2.6\xc2\xa0million.\n       <a href="/wiki/Berwick_High_School_(Louisiana)" title="Berwick High School (Louisiana)">\n        Berwick High School\n       </a>\n       , sheltering about 2,000\xc2\xa0people, was deroofed during the storm. Generally, single-family homes fared well, with most losing only roofing shingles, though others suffered severe damage after large trees fell on them. In\n       <a href="/wiki/Cypremort_Point_State_Park" title="Cypremort Point State Park">\n        Cypremort Point State Park\n       </a>\n       , several mobile homes were destroyed.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75">\n        <a href="#cite_note-75">\n         [71]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Houses in Berwick, Morgan City, and\n       <a href="/wiki/Patterson,_Louisiana" title="Patterson, Louisiana">\n        Patterson\n       </a>\n       suffered major damage. Throughout the parish, 1,367\xc2\xa0dwellings were destroyed, 2,028\xc2\xa0were severely damaged, and 4,770\xc2\xa0others were impacted to a minor degree. Property damage alone in St. Mary Parish reached approximately $150\xc2\xa0million.\n       <a href="/wiki/Iberia_Parish,_Louisiana" title="Iberia Parish, Louisiana">\n        Iberia Parish\n       </a>\n       was also among the most severely impacted parishes. Two schools collectively sheltering about 3,600\xc2\xa0people in Jeanerette and New Iberia lost their roofs. One death occurred in the parish due to electrocution. A total of 407\xc2\xa0residences were demolished, 2,528\xc2\xa0others were extensively damaged, and 3,526\xc2\xa0others were inflicted with minor damage. Overall, the parish suffered $125\xc2\xa0million in property damage, while an additional $200\xc2\xa0million in damage was inflicted on sugar crops.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ncdc_74-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ncdc-74">\n         [70]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Across the state, the hurricane damaged 23,000\xc2\xa0homes and destroyed 985\xc2\xa0homes and 1,951\xc2\xa0mobile homes; private property damage was estimated at $1\xc2\xa0billion. The high winds destroyed large areas of sugar and soybean crops, estimated at $289\xc2\xa0million in damage.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ncdc_74-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ncdc-74">\n         [70]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Strong winds also left at least 230,000\xc2\xa0people without electricity.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-applebome_76-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-applebome-76">\n         [72]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       During the storm\'s passage, upwelling occurred in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Atchafalaya_Basin" title="Atchafalaya Basin">\n        Atchafalaya Basin\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Bayou_Lafourche" title="Bayou Lafourche">\n        Bayou Lafourche\n       </a>\n       , killing 187\xc2\xa0million freshwater fish. Damage to the fishing industry was estimated at $266\xc2\xa0million. Overall, losses in the state of Louisiana reached approximately $1.56\xc2\xa0billion.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ncdc_74-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ncdc-74">\n         [70]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       A total of 17\xc2\xa0deaths occurred in Louisiana, 8\xc2\xa0directly and 9\xc2\xa0from indirect causes.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tcr_2-39">\n        <a href="#cite_note-tcr-2">\n         [1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       At least 75\xc2\xa0injuries were reported.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77">\n        <a href="#cite_note-77">\n         [73]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Remainder_of_the_United_States">\n        Remainder of the United States\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Andrew&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Remainder of the United States">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:292px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Andrew_1992_rainfall.gif">\n         <img alt="A map of the United States showing various rainfall totals by color code" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="914" data-file-width="1014" height="261" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Andrew_1992_rainfall.gif/290px-Andrew_1992_rainfall.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Andrew_1992_rainfall.gif/435px-Andrew_1992_rainfall.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Andrew_1992_rainfall.gif/580px-Andrew_1992_rainfall.gif 2x" width="290"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Andrew_1992_rainfall.gif" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Rainfall summary of Hurricane Andrew in the United States\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       While Andrew was entering the Gulf of Mexico, oil companies evacuated hundreds of employees from offshore drilling platforms.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78">\n        <a href="#cite_note-78">\n         [74]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The storm damaged 241\xc2\xa0oil and gas facilities and toppled 33\xc2\xa0platforms off the coast of Louisiana,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ngi_79-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ngi-79">\n         [75]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       causing significant disruptions in production. Additionally, 83\xc2\xa0pipeline segments suffered damage to some degree. The oil industry lost about $12\xc2\xa0million per day in the days following Andrew and $4\xc2\xa0million daily by three weeks later.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ngi_79-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ngi-79">\n         [75]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Initially, a production loss of 240,000 to 270,000\xc2\xa0barrels per day occurred \xe2\x80\x93 approximately one-third of production throughout the Gulf of Mexico.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80">\n        <a href="#cite_note-80">\n         [76]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Overall, Hurricane Andrew caused about $500\xc2\xa0million in damage to oil facilities.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tcr_2-40">\n        <a href="#cite_note-tcr-2">\n         [1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       As Andrew moved ashore in Louisiana, its outer fringes produced a storm tide of about 1.3\xc2\xa0ft (0.40\xc2\xa0m) in\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sabine_Pass,_Texas" title="Sabine Pass, Texas">\n        Sabine Pass, Texas\n       </a>\n       . Winds were generally light in the state, reaching 30\xc2\xa0mph (48\xc2\xa0km/h) in\n       <a href="/wiki/Port_Arthur,_Texas" title="Port Arthur, Texas">\n        Port Arthur\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tcr_2-41">\n        <a href="#cite_note-tcr-2">\n         [1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       As Andrew crossed into Mississippi, 3\n       <a href="/wiki/Severe_thunderstorm_warning" title="Severe thunderstorm warning">\n        severe thunderstorm warnings\n       </a>\n       , 21\n       <a href="/wiki/Tornado_warning" title="Tornado warning">\n        tornado warnings\n       </a>\n       , and 16\n       <a href="/wiki/Flood_warning" title="Flood warning">\n        flood warnings\n       </a>\n       were issued.\n       <a href="/wiki/Funnel_cloud" title="Funnel cloud">\n        Funnel clouds\n       </a>\n       were observed near the path of the storm,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jackson_81-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-jackson-81">\n         [77]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       along with 26\xc2\xa0tornadoes.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82">\n        <a href="#cite_note-82">\n         [78]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Structural damage was generally minimal, occurring from the tornadoes and severe thunderstorms. One tornado in\n       <a href="/wiki/Kemper_County,_Mississippi" title="Kemper County, Mississippi">\n        Kemper County\n       </a>\n       destroyed a mobile home, while another twister in\n       <a href="/wiki/Lauderdale_County,_Mississippi" title="Lauderdale County, Mississippi">\n        Lauderdale County\n       </a>\n       demolished a mobile home, damaged five other dwellings, and injured four people.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jackson3_83-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-jackson3-83">\n         [79]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Additionally, a possible tornado damaged a home and two trailers in\n       <a href="/wiki/Lawrence_County,_Mississippi" title="Lawrence County, Mississippi">\n        Lawrence County\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jackson_81-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-jackson-81">\n         [77]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Strong winds knocked down trees in the southwestern portion of the state.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jackson_81-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-jackson-81">\n         [77]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Much of Mississippi received 3 to 5\xc2\xa0in (76 to 127\xc2\xa0mm) of rain, while areas near the southwest corner of the state observed over 7\xc2\xa0in (180\xc2\xa0mm) of precipitation,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jackson2_84-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-jackson2-84">\n         [80]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       with a peak of 9.30\xc2\xa0in (236\xc2\xa0mm) at\n       <a href="/wiki/Sumrall,_Mississippi" title="Sumrall, Mississippi">\n        Sumrall\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gulfrain_85-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-gulfrain-85">\n         [81]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Flooding was mostly limited to the inundation of minor roads and low-lying areas in several counties.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jackson2_84-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-jackson2-84">\n         [80]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In Alabama, precipitation amounts in the state peaked at 4.71\xc2\xa0in (120\xc2\xa0mm) in\n       <a href="/wiki/Aliceville,_Alabama" title="Aliceville, Alabama">\n        Aliceville\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gulfrain_85-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-gulfrain-85">\n         [81]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The rainfall caused flooding in low-lying areas and creeks, covering a few county roads but not entering many houses or businesses.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jackson2_84-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-jackson2-84">\n         [80]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Along the coast, the storm produced flooding and high tides.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-al_31-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-al-31">\n         [29]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Along\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dauphin_Island" title="Dauphin Island">\n        Dauphin Island\n       </a>\n       , high tides left severe beach erosion, with portions of the island losing up to 30\xc2\xa0ft (9.1\xc2\xa0m) of sand.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-al_31-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-al-31">\n         [29]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Three damaging tornadoes occurred in the state. The most damaging tornado was spawned in\n       <a href="/wiki/Elmore_County,_Alabama" title="Elmore County, Alabama">\n        Elmore County\n       </a>\n       and moved from an area northeast of\n       <a href="/wiki/Montgomery,_Alabama" title="Montgomery, Alabama">\n        Montgomery\n       </a>\n       to the south of\n       <a href="/wiki/Wetumpka,_Alabama" title="Wetumpka, Alabama">\n        Wetumpka\n       </a>\n       and briefly lifted during its 0.5\xc2\xa0mi (0.80\xc2\xa0km) track. The tornado destroyed 2\xc2\xa0homes and damaged 18\xc2\xa0homes, 1\xc2\xa0mobile home, 2\xc2\xa0barns, and 1\xc2\xa0vehicle. One person was injured by the twister.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ncdc_74-4">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ncdc-74">\n         [70]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Sustained winds in the state were below tropical storm force, though a wind gust of 41 mph (67 km/h) was observed in\n       <a href="/wiki/Huntsville,_Alabama" title="Huntsville, Alabama">\n        Huntsville\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tcr_2-42">\n        <a href="#cite_note-tcr-2">\n         [1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Although 48\n       <a href="/wiki/List_of_counties_in_Alabama" title="List of counties in Alabama">\n        counties in Alabama\n       </a>\n       reported wind damage, impact across the state was generally minor.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-al_31-4">\n        <a href="#cite_note-al-31">\n         [29]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Tropical storm force wind gusts and damaging tornadoes extended eastward into Georgia. Several\n       <a href="/wiki/List_of_counties_in_Georgia_(U.S._state)" title="List of counties in Georgia (U.S. state)">\n        counties\n       </a>\n       in the northwest and west-central portions of the state reported downed trees and tree limbs and fallen power lines, causing scattered power outages, but structural damage was generally minor. In\n       <a href="/wiki/Carroll_County,_Georgia" title="Carroll County, Georgia">\n        Carroll County\n       </a>\n       , several dwellings and barns were damaged, with one mobile home destroyed. At the\n       <a href="/wiki/Columbus_Metropolitan_Airport" title="Columbus Metropolitan Airport">\n        Columbus Metropolitan Airport\n       </a>\n       , buildings, billboards, and signs were damaged. Additionally, a tornado in\n       <a href="/wiki/Floyd_County,_Georgia" title="Floyd County, Georgia">\n        Floyd County\n       </a>\n       near\n       <a href="/wiki/Rome,_Georgia" title="Rome, Georgia">\n        Rome\n       </a>\n       snapped and uprooted several trees, damaged several fences and homes, and flipped over a trailer, tossing it on top of four cars.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ncdc_74-5">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ncdc-74">\n         [70]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Monetary losses in the state reached about $100,000.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tcr_2-43">\n        <a href="#cite_note-tcr-2">\n         [1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In\n       <a href="/wiki/Tennessee" title="Tennessee">\n        Tennessee\n       </a>\n       , thunderstorm winds and tornadoes associated with Andrew downed trees and power lines, but caused little overall impact to homes and buildings. Similarly, in\n       <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina" title="North Carolina">\n        North Carolina\n       </a>\n       , thunderstorm winds toppled trees and power lines at a number of locations in the mountainous areas of the state, especially in\n       <a href="/wiki/Avery_County,_North_Carolina" title="Avery County, North Carolina">\n        Avery County\n       </a>\n       . Rainfall from Andrew spread across the southeastern United States along the\n       <a href="/wiki/Appalachian_Mountains" title="Appalachian Mountains">\n        Appalachian Mountains\n       </a>\n       corridor; totals of over 5\xc2\xa0in (125\xc2\xa0mm) were reported where Georgia and South Carolina meet North Carolina.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rain_15-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-rain-15">\n         [13]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In\n       <a href="/wiki/West_Virginia" title="West Virginia">\n        West Virginia\n       </a>\n       , the remnants of Andrew combined with a cold front to produce 1.5 to 2.5\xc2\xa0in (38 to 64\xc2\xa0mm) of rain over portions of the state, causing flooding in areas of\n       <a href="/wiki/Morgantown,_West_Virginia" title="Morgantown, West Virginia">\n        Morgantown\n       </a>\n       with poor drainage. The remnants of Andrew also spawned several tornadoes in\n       <a href="/wiki/Maryland" title="Maryland">\n        Maryland\n       </a>\n       . A tornado in\n       <a href="/wiki/Howard_County,_Maryland" title="Howard County, Maryland">\n        Howard County\n       </a>\n       damaged several homes, some extensively. The twister also tossed and wrecked a recreational vehicle and its trailer, downed trees, and flattened cornfields.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ncdc_74-6">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ncdc-74">\n         [70]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Precipitation continued along the path of Andrew\'s remnants through the Mid-Atlantic and Ohio Valley, with precipitation measured as far north as\n       <a href="/wiki/Upstate_New_York" title="Upstate New York">\n        Upstate New York\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rain_15-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-rain-15">\n         [13]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Aftermath">\n        Aftermath\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Andrew&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Aftermath">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/List_of_retired_Atlantic_hurricane_names" title="List of retired Atlantic hurricane names">\n        List of retired Atlantic hurricane names\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone_naming#Retirement" title="Tropical cyclone naming">\n        Tropical cyclone naming \xc2\xa7\xc2\xa0Retirement\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       After the season had ended, the World Meteorological Organization\'s RA IV Hurricane Committee retired the name\n       <i>\n        Andrew\n       </i>\n       from the list of future names for Atlantic tropical cyclones and replaced it with\n       <i>\n        Alex.\n       </i>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86">\n        <a href="#cite_note-86">\n         [82]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-about_names_87-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-about_names-87">\n         [83]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The name\n       <i>\n        Andrew\n       </i>\n       will never be used again for another Atlantic Hurricane.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Bahamas_3">\n        Bahamas\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Andrew&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Bahamas">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Initially, the Bahamas National Disaster Coordinator believed that\n       <a href="/wiki/Emergency_management" title="Emergency management">\n        foreign aid\n       </a>\n       was not required, but shortly after the storm, the\n       <a href="/wiki/Government_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Government of the United Kingdom">\n        Government of the United Kingdom\n       </a>\n       began distributing blankets, food, ice, and water.\n       <a href="/wiki/HMS_Cardiff_(D108)" title="HMS Cardiff (D108)">\n        HMS\n        <i>\n         Cardiff\n        </i>\n       </a>\n       , a\n       <a href="/wiki/Royal_Navy" title="Royal Navy">\n        Royal Navy\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Type_42_destroyer" title="Type 42 destroyer">\n        Type 42 destroyer\n       </a>\n       , was the operational guard ship at the time and assisted in relief operations in and around the Gregorytown area.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wp_19-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-wp-19">\n         [17]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rw_48-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-rw-48">\n         [45]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In addition, assistance came from Canada, Japan, and the United States, as well as the\n       <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">\n        United Nations\n       </a>\n       . The\n       <a href="/wiki/American_Red_Cross" title="American Red Cross">\n        American Red Cross\n       </a>\n       delivered 100\xc2\xa0tents, 100\xc2\xa0rolls of plastic sheeting, and 1,000\xc2\xa0cots.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rw_48-4">\n        <a href="#cite_note-rw-48">\n         [45]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Rebuilding began quickly on the hardest hit islands. However, trees and vegetation were expected to take years to recover. Despite reconstruction efforts and the small number of resort lodgings affected (around 2%), officials expected a 10%\xe2\x80\x9320% decline in tourism.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nyt_50-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-nyt-50">\n         [47]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Government_of_the_Bahamas" title="Government of the Bahamas">\n        Bahamian Government\n       </a>\n       , observing that their response mechanisms were not sufficient, reformed the National Emergency and Management Agency.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88">\n        <a href="#cite_note-88">\n         [84]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="United_States">\n        United States\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Andrew&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: United States">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:FEMA_-_1926_-_Photograph_by_Bob_Epstein_taken_on_08-24-1992_in_Florida.jpg">\n         <img alt="A sign indicating a relief camp providing water for cleaning and drinking" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1952" data-file-width="2940" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/FEMA_-_1926_-_Photograph_by_Bob_Epstein_taken_on_08-24-1992_in_Florida.jpg/220px-FEMA_-_1926_-_Photograph_by_Bob_Epstein_taken_on_08-24-1992_in_Florida.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/FEMA_-_1926_-_Photograph_by_Bob_Epstein_taken_on_08-24-1992_in_Florida.jpg/330px-FEMA_-_1926_-_Photograph_by_Bob_Epstein_taken_on_08-24-1992_in_Florida.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/FEMA_-_1926_-_Photograph_by_Bob_Epstein_taken_on_08-24-1992_in_Florida.jpg/440px-FEMA_-_1926_-_Photograph_by_Bob_Epstein_taken_on_08-24-1992_in_Florida.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:FEMA_-_1926_-_Photograph_by_Bob_Epstein_taken_on_08-24-1992_in_Florida.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Sign pointing in the direction of a relief camp in South Florida\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       After assessing the devastation in Florida and Louisiana,\n       <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_United_States" title="President of the United States">\n        U.S. President\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/George_H._W._Bush" title="George H. W. Bush">\n        George H. W. Bush\n       </a>\n       initially proposed a $7.1\xc2\xa0billion aid package to provide disaster benefits, small-business loans, agricultural recovery, food stamps, and public housing for victims of Hurricane Andrew.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nyt-gs_89-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-nyt-gs-89">\n         [85]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       After the\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_House_of_Representatives" title="United States House of Representatives">\n        House of Representatives\n       </a>\n       appropriated aid to victims of\n       <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Iniki" title="Hurricane Iniki">\n        Hurricane Iniki\n       </a>\n       in\n       <a href="/wiki/Hawaii" title="Hawaii">\n        Hawaii\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Typhoon_Omar" title="Typhoon Omar">\n        Typhoon Omar\n       </a>\n       in\n       <a href="/wiki/Guam" title="Guam">\n        Guam\n       </a>\n       , the cost was later increased to $11.1\xc2\xa0billion. The bill, which was the most costly disaster aid package at the time, was passed by\n       <a href="/wiki/102nd_United_States_Congress" title="102nd United States Congress">\n        Congress\n       </a>\n       as House Resolution\xc2\xa05620 on September\xc2\xa018,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-os_90-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-os-90">\n         [86]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and signed into law by President Bush on September\xc2\xa023.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hr5620_91-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-hr5620-91">\n         [87]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The state of Florida alone received $9\xc2\xa0billion through the disaster relief bill.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92">\n        <a href="#cite_note-92">\n         [88]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Federal_Emergency_Management_Agency" title="Federal Emergency Management Agency">\n        Federal Emergency Management Agency\n       </a>\n       (FEMA) was criticized for its slow response in both Florida and Louisiana. Even a month prior to Andrew, the\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_House_Committee_on_Appropriations" title="United States House Committee on Appropriations">\n        House Committee on Appropriations\n       </a>\n       \xe2\x80\x93 which oversees the budget for FEMA \xe2\x80\x93 released a report calling the agency a "political dumping ground" and a "turkey farm" due to its "weak, inexperienced leaders". Congressman\n       <a href="/wiki/S._William_Green" title="S. William Green">\n        S. William Green\n       </a>\n       of\n       <a href="/wiki/New_York_(state)" title="New York (state)">\n        New York\n       </a>\n       , a member of the Appropriations Committee, stated that he believed the agency learned little from its botched response to\n       <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Hugo" title="Hurricane Hugo">\n        Hurricane Hugo\n       </a>\n       in 1989. However, Green also criticized local officials for expecting "them [FEMA] to come and run the whole show". Some FEMA officials responded that it was impossible to respond as they had been requested while also continuing to provide aid for the\n       <a href="/wiki/1992_Los_Angeles_riots" title="1992 Los Angeles riots">\n        Los Angeles riots\n       </a>\n       . FEMA spokesman Grant Peterson stated, "24 hours is not reasonable to expect to have all the resources of the federal government landing in the middle of a disaster."\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93">\n        <a href="#cite_note-93">\n         [89]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Florida_3">\n        Florida\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Andrew&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Florida">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <p>\n       In Florida, President Bush assessed damage in areas south of Miami with Florida Governor\n       <a href="/wiki/Lawton_Chiles" title="Lawton Chiles">\n        Lawton Chiles\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mt2_55-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-mt2-55">\n         [51]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The president quickly declared the region a disaster area, which provided public assistance to victims of the storm in Broward, Collier, Dade, and Monroe Counties.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94">\n        <a href="#cite_note-94">\n         [90]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/Lieutenant_Governor_of_Florida" title="Lieutenant Governor of Florida">\n        Lieutenant Governor\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Buddy_MacKay" title="Buddy MacKay">\n        Buddy MacKay\n       </a>\n       flew over the impact area and described the scene as looking "like a war zone".\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dn0827p2.gif_95-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-dn0827p2.gif-95">\n         [91]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Governor Chiles considered asking the\n       <a href="/wiki/Florida_Legislature" title="Florida Legislature">\n        Florida State Legislature\n       </a>\n       to raise taxes, stating that "No matter how much Congress appropriates to repair damage from Hurricane Andrew, the state will face a substantial cleanup bill".\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nyt-gs_89-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-nyt-gs-89">\n         [85]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Instead of raising taxes, Chiles signed a bill into law on December\xc2\xa017 that created a three-year reserve fund for losses to uninsured businesses and homes, as well as government and school buildings and functions. Additionally, the bill allowed South Floridians to keep an estimated $500\xc2\xa0million in sales tax generated by rebuilding efforts.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96">\n        <a href="#cite_note-96">\n         [92]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:FEMA_-_2378_-_Photograph_by_Bob_Epstein_taken_on_08-24-1992_in_Florida.jpg">\n         <img alt="People working to clear debris off of a damaged home" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1952" data-file-width="2940" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/FEMA_-_2378_-_Photograph_by_Bob_Epstein_taken_on_08-24-1992_in_Florida.jpg/220px-FEMA_-_2378_-_Photograph_by_Bob_Epstein_taken_on_08-24-1992_in_Florida.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/FEMA_-_2378_-_Photograph_by_Bob_Epstein_taken_on_08-24-1992_in_Florida.jpg/330px-FEMA_-_2378_-_Photograph_by_Bob_Epstein_taken_on_08-24-1992_in_Florida.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/FEMA_-_2378_-_Photograph_by_Bob_Epstein_taken_on_08-24-1992_in_Florida.jpg/440px-FEMA_-_2378_-_Photograph_by_Bob_Epstein_taken_on_08-24-1992_in_Florida.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:FEMA_-_2378_-_Photograph_by_Bob_Epstein_taken_on_08-24-1992_in_Florida.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Clean-up after Hurricane Andrew in\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dade_County,_Florida" title="Dade County, Florida">\n          Dade County\n         </a>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Crime, especially looting and theft, rose sharply in the areas south of Miami immediately after Andrew. Reports indicate that merchandise was stolen at damaged or destroyed shopping centers in southern Dade County. Additionally, looting occurred in neighborhoods severely affected by the storm, even in homes where few possessions remained.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SPT_64-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-SPT-64">\n         [60]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97">\n        <a href="#cite_note-97">\n         [93]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Initially, the slow response of federal aid prompted Dade County Emergency Management Director Kate Hale to famously exclaim at a nationally televised news conference, "Where in the hell is the cavalry on this one? They keep saying we\'re going to get supplies. For God\'s sake, where are they?" Almost immediately, President Bush promised, "Help is on the way," and mobile kitchens, food, and tents, along with over 20,000 units from the\n       <a href="/wiki/Florida_Army_National_Guard" title="Florida Army National Guard">\n        Florida Army National Guard\n       </a>\n       (\n       <a href="/wiki/124th_Infantry_Regiment_(United_States)" title="124th Infantry Regiment (United States)">\n        124th Infantry Regiment\n       </a>\n       from Florida); the\n       <a href="/wiki/24th_Infantry_Division_(United_States)" title="24th Infantry Division (United States)">\n        24th Infantry Division\n       </a>\n       from\n       <a href="/wiki/Fort_Stewart" title="Fort Stewart">\n        Fort Stewart\n       </a>\n       , the\n       <a href="/wiki/82nd_Airborne_Division" title="82nd Airborne Division">\n        82nd Airborne Division\n       </a>\n       in\n       <a href="/wiki/Fort_Bragg" title="Fort Bragg">\n        Fort Bragg\n       </a>\n       , and the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/10th_Mountain_Division_(United_States)" title="10th Mountain Division (United States)">\n        10th Mountain Division\n       </a>\n       from\n       <a href="/wiki/Fort_Drum" title="Fort Drum">\n        Fort Drum\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-St._Petersburg_Times_98-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-St._Petersburg_Times-98">\n         [94]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99">\n        <a href="#cite_note-99">\n         [95]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In order to provide temporary housing for the homeless, military personnel initially set up a total of five tent cities in\n       <a href="/wiki/Florida_City,_Florida" title="Florida City, Florida">\n        Florida City\n       </a>\n       and Homestead,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100">\n        <a href="#cite_note-100">\n         [96]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       while a sixth tent city was opened at the\n       <a href="/wiki/Miccosukee_Indian_Reservation" title="Miccosukee Indian Reservation">\n        Miccosukee Indian Reservation\n       </a>\n       shortly after\n       <a href="/wiki/Labor_Day" title="Labor Day">\n        Labor Day\n       </a>\n       weekend.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Miccosukee_101-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Miccosukee-101">\n         [97]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Canada" title="Government of Canada">\n        Government of Canada\n       </a>\n       dispatched a team 90\n       <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Armed_Forces" title="Canadian Armed Forces">\n        military\n       </a>\n       engineers to repair community centers, hospitals, and schools. Additionally, a crew of 300\xc2\xa0military personnel were sent to Miami via the\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/HMCS_Protecteur_(AOR_509)" title="HMCS Protecteur (AOR 509)">\n         HMCS Protecteur\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       to assist American relief teams.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102">\n        <a href="#cite_note-102">\n         [98]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The storm struck Florida in the midst of\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_1992" title="United States presidential election, 1992">\n        1992 presidential election campaign\n       </a>\n       . A poll conducted by\n       <a href="/wiki/CBS_News" title="CBS News">\n        CBS News\n       </a>\n       in September showed that 65% of Dade County residents approved of Bush\'s handling of the disaster, while 61% of residents approved statewide. Despite the support of Bush\'s response and his proposal to rebuild Homestead Air Force Base, he benefited little politically and trailed 48%\xe2\x80\x9342% against\n       <a href="/wiki/Bill_Clinton" title="Bill Clinton">\n        Bill Clinton\n       </a>\n       in another poll taken in September. Additionally, 75% of voters in Dade County and 82% of Floridians overall stated that the president\'s actions in response to Andrew would not impact their vote in November.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103">\n        <a href="#cite_note-103">\n         [99]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Bush went on to\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election_in_Florida,_1992" title="United States presidential election in Florida, 1992">\n        carry the state of Florida\n       </a>\n       , but by a margin of only 1.89%.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104">\n        <a href="#cite_note-104">\n         [100]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The hurricane also impacted Governor Chiles politically. The state\'s response to the storm was perceived as poor, sinking Chiles\' approval rating to 22%, while his disapproval rating rose to 76%. However, Chiles was able to recover prior to the\n       <a href="/wiki/Florida_gubernatorial_election,_1994" title="Florida gubernatorial election, 1994">\n        1994 gubernatorial election\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105">\n        <a href="#cite_note-105">\n         [101]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In the aftermath of the storm, extensive psychological effects were documented. Difficulty during clean-up and recovery lead to increased divorce rates and a spike in\n       <a href="/wiki/Posttraumatic_stress_disorder" title="Posttraumatic stress disorder">\n        posttraumatic stress disorder\n       </a>\n       (PTSD). The cases of PTSD primarily impacted children. A sampling of 378\xc2\xa0adolescents by the\n       <a href="/wiki/University_of_South_Carolina" title="University of South Carolina">\n        University of South Carolina\n       </a>\n       \'s Department of Epidemiology and Biostatistics indicated that 3% of males and 9% of females met the criteria for PTSD.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106">\n        <a href="#cite_note-106">\n         [102]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Dozens of children in the area attempted suicide, while counselors reported that between 50 and 60\xc2\xa0children discussed killing themselves between December\xc2\xa01992 and January\xc2\xa01993.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107">\n        <a href="#cite_note-107">\n         [103]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       A panel of psychiatrists and psychologists at the\n       <a href="/wiki/University_of_Miami" title="University of Miami">\n        University of Miami\n       </a>\n       agreed that as many as 90% of residents in the worst impacted areas would experience at least a few symptoms of PTSD.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108">\n        <a href="#cite_note-108">\n         [104]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Within six months, the circumstances related to the aftermath of Andrew led to at least five suicides and four homicides.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109">\n        <a href="#cite_note-109">\n         [105]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:FEMA_-_2399_-_Photograph_by_Bob_Epstein_taken_on_08-24-1992_in_Florida.jpg">\n         <img alt="A heavily damaged home with much of its brick exterior and roof destroyed" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1952" data-file-width="2940" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/FEMA_-_2399_-_Photograph_by_Bob_Epstein_taken_on_08-24-1992_in_Florida.jpg/220px-FEMA_-_2399_-_Photograph_by_Bob_Epstein_taken_on_08-24-1992_in_Florida.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/FEMA_-_2399_-_Photograph_by_Bob_Epstein_taken_on_08-24-1992_in_Florida.jpg/330px-FEMA_-_2399_-_Photograph_by_Bob_Epstein_taken_on_08-24-1992_in_Florida.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/FEMA_-_2399_-_Photograph_by_Bob_Epstein_taken_on_08-24-1992_in_Florida.jpg/440px-FEMA_-_2399_-_Photograph_by_Bob_Epstein_taken_on_08-24-1992_in_Florida.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:FEMA_-_2399_-_Photograph_by_Bob_Epstein_taken_on_08-24-1992_in_Florida.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         A home destroyed by the storm\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Although proposals to rebuild Homestead Air Force Base were initially rejected,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-homesteadafbclosing_61-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-homesteadafbclosing-61">\n         [57]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       the\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Defense" title="United States Department of Defense">\n        United States Department of Defense\n       </a>\n       eventually expended over $100\xc2\xa0million to begin repairs. Unsalvageable buildings were demolished. Reconstruction then began on a\n       <a href="/wiki/Florida_Air_National_Guard" title="Florida Air National Guard">\n        Florida Air National Guard\n       </a>\n       tower, air traffic control tower, and maintenance hangars. Next, the rebuilding of communications, medical, security facility, vehicle maintenance, and wing headquarters buildings began. On March\xc2\xa05, 1994, the base reopened as Homestead Air Reserve Base.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110">\n        <a href="#cite_note-110">\n         [106]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Prior to Andrew, the base employed approximately 6,500\xc2\xa0military personnel and 1,000\xc2\xa0civilians and annually added about $450\xc2\xa0million to the local economy.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111">\n        <a href="#cite_note-111">\n         [107]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reserve_112-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-reserve-112">\n         [108]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       After its reopening,\n       <a href="/wiki/Major_(United_States)" title="Major (United States)">\n        Major\n       </a>\n       Bobby D\'Angelo expected the base to annually contribute less than half of that \xe2\x80\x93 between $180\xc2\xa0million and $200\xc2\xa0million.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reserve_112-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-reserve-112">\n         [108]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The city of Homestead spent about $6\xc2\xa0million on rebuilding the\n       <a href="/wiki/Homestead_Sports_Complex" title="Homestead Sports Complex">\n        Homestead Sports Complex\n       </a>\n       . Despite this, the\n       <a href="/wiki/Cleveland_Indians" title="Cleveland Indians">\n        Cleveland Indians\n       </a>\n       , fearing the relocation of their more affluent fans, moved their\n       <a href="/wiki/Spring_training" title="Spring training">\n        spring training\n       </a>\n       location to\n       <a href="/wiki/Chain_of_Lakes_Park" title="Chain of Lakes Park">\n        Chain of Lakes Park\n       </a>\n       in\n       <a href="/wiki/Winter_Haven,_Florida" title="Winter Haven, Florida">\n        Winter Haven\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-maines_113-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-maines-113">\n         [109]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114">\n        <a href="#cite_note-114">\n         [110]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       As homes were being rebuilt, FEMA provided free temporary mobile homes for 3,501\xc2\xa0families and financial assistance to more than 40,000\xc2\xa0other families for staying in hotel rooms, paying rent, and repairing homes.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115">\n        <a href="#cite_note-115">\n         [111]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Nearly two years after Andrew, about 70% of homes in Homestead that were damaged or destroyed were repaired or rebuilt. Additionally, of the homes destroyed or severely damaged throughout Dade County, 36,000\xc2\xa0had been restored by July 1994.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116">\n        <a href="#cite_note-116">\n         [112]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       More than 930,000\xc2\xa0policyholders in South Florida lost coverage after 11\xc2\xa0insurance companies went bankrupt, caused by more than 600,000\xc2\xa0insurance claims filed. This led the Florida Legislature to create new entities, such as the Joint Underwriting Association, the Florida Windstorm Underwriting Association, and the Florida Hurricane Catastrophe Fund, in an effort to restore adequate insurance capacity.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117">\n        <a href="#cite_note-117">\n         [113]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Stricter building codes were created in Florida in the aftermath of Hurricane Andrew. A survey by Tim Marshall and Richard Herzog of the Haag Engineer Company in\n       <a href="/wiki/Carrollton,_Texas" title="Carrollton, Texas">\n        Carrollton, Texas\n       </a>\n       , highlighted several construction issues. On the roof of some homes, the concrete tiles were glued to felt paper, which could easily be ripped by straight line winds. At houses with shingled roofs, it was found that some of the shingles were stapled perpendicular to the long axis, also allowing them to be torn away. After the tiles or shingles were peeled off, the plywood and prefabricated trusses were exposed to the weather. Eventually, the plywood and the trusses suffered structural failure, leading to roof collapses.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118">\n        <a href="#cite_note-118">\n         [114]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:FEMA_-_2599_-_Photograph_by_Bob_Epstein_taken_on_08-24-1992_in_Florida.jpg">\n         <img alt="Aerial view of a large number of temporary housing tents positioned throughout several baseball fields" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1952" data-file-width="2940" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/FEMA_-_2599_-_Photograph_by_Bob_Epstein_taken_on_08-24-1992_in_Florida.jpg/220px-FEMA_-_2599_-_Photograph_by_Bob_Epstein_taken_on_08-24-1992_in_Florida.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/FEMA_-_2599_-_Photograph_by_Bob_Epstein_taken_on_08-24-1992_in_Florida.jpg/330px-FEMA_-_2599_-_Photograph_by_Bob_Epstein_taken_on_08-24-1992_in_Florida.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/FEMA_-_2599_-_Photograph_by_Bob_Epstein_taken_on_08-24-1992_in_Florida.jpg/440px-FEMA_-_2599_-_Photograph_by_Bob_Epstein_taken_on_08-24-1992_in_Florida.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:FEMA_-_2599_-_Photograph_by_Bob_Epstein_taken_on_08-24-1992_in_Florida.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Tent cities were constructed to house displaced residents.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       In July\xc2\xa01996, Governor Chiles established the Florida Building Codes Study Commission, with the purpose of assessing the building codes at the time, as well as enacting improvements and reform to the system. The commission study indicated that building codes and regulations were developed, amended, and administered by over 400\xc2\xa0local jurisdictions and state agencies.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119">\n        <a href="#cite_note-119">\n         [115]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The Florida Building Code was established in 1998 and put into effect by 2002.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120">\n        <a href="#cite_note-120">\n         [116]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       It phased out local laws and regulations and replaced them with universal statewide building codes. After hurricanes\n       <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Charley" title="Hurricane Charley">\n        Charley\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Frances" title="Hurricane Frances">\n        Frances\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Ivan" title="Hurricane Ivan">\n        Ivan\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Jeanne" title="Hurricane Jeanne">\n        Jeanne\n       </a>\n       in\n       <a href="/wiki/2004_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="2004 Atlantic hurricane season">\n        2004\n       </a>\n       , a study conducted by the\n       <a href="/wiki/University_of_Florida" title="University of Florida">\n        University of Florida\n       </a>\n       in the following year noted that "Homes built under the new Florida Building Code that became effective in 2002 sustained less damage on average than those built between 1994 and 2001." A report by the Florida Legislature in 2006 after hurricanes\n       <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Dennis" title="Hurricane Dennis">\n        Dennis\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Katrina" title="Hurricane Katrina">\n        Katrina\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Wilma" title="Hurricane Wilma">\n        Wilma\n       </a>\n       in\n       <a href="/wiki/2005_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="2005 Atlantic hurricane season">\n        2005\n       </a>\n       came to a similar conclusion, indicating that "they added further evidence that the Florida Building Code is working."\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121">\n        <a href="#cite_note-121">\n         [117]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The hurricane also transformed the demographics of Dade County. A migration of mostly White families northward to Broward and Palm Beach County was ongoing, but accelerated after Andrew.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-growing_populations_122-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-growing_populations-122">\n         [118]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Many of these families had used the money they received from insurance claims to relocate.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kershaw14_123-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-kershaw14-123">\n         [119]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The population growth was especially noticeable in southwestern Broward County, where land development was pushed "years ahead of schedule".\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-growing_populations_122-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-growing_populations-122">\n         [118]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Similar migration occurred within the Jewish community. Although there are areas of Dade County that still have significant Jewish populations, many Jews resettled to\n       <a href="/wiki/Coral_Springs,_Florida" title="Coral Springs, Florida">\n        Coral Springs\n       </a>\n       , west\n       <a href="/wiki/Fort_Lauderdale,_Florida" title="Fort Lauderdale, Florida">\n        Fort Lauderdale\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Hallandale_Beach,_Florida" title="Hallandale Beach, Florida">\n        Hallandale Beach\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Plantation,_Florida" title="Plantation, Florida">\n        Plantation\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Tamarac,_Florida" title="Tamarac, Florida">\n        Tamarac\n       </a>\n       in Broward County and\n       <a href="/wiki/Boca_Raton,_Florida" title="Boca Raton, Florida">\n        Boca Raton\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/West_Palm_Beach,_Florida" title="West Palm Beach, Florida">\n        West Palm Beach\n       </a>\n       in Palm Beach County.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124">\n        <a href="#cite_note-124">\n         [120]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The county had a net loss of about 36,000\xc2\xa0people in 1992, while Broward and Palm Beach counties gained about 17,000 and 2,300\xc2\xa0Dade County residents, respectively.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-maines_113-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-maines-113">\n         [109]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       By 2001, 230,710\xc2\xa0people had moved from Dade County to Broward County, while 29,125\xc2\xa0Dade County residents had moved to Palm Beach County. However, as Broward County became more crowded, 100,871\xc2\xa0people relocated from Broward County to Palm Beach County.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125">\n        <a href="#cite_note-125">\n         [121]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Consequently, the Hispanic population in south Dade County climbed rapidly.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kershaw14_123-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-kershaw14-123">\n         [119]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In Homestead, for example, the Latino population increased from 30% to 45% between 1990 and 2000.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126">\n        <a href="#cite_note-126">\n         [122]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       During the storm, a facility housing\n       <a href="/wiki/Burmese_python" title="Burmese python">\n        Burmese pythons\n       </a>\n       was destroyed, allowing many of them to escape into the Everglades. Although Burmese pythons \xe2\x80\x93 native to\n       <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asia" title="Southeast Asia">\n        Southeast Asia\n       </a>\n       \xe2\x80\x93 had been sighted in Everglades National Park since the 1980s, the destruction of this facility contributed significantly to\n       <a href="/wiki/Burmese_pythons_in_Florida" title="Burmese pythons in Florida">\n        the establishment of breeding populations in Florida\n       </a>\n       . Due to rapid reproduction and ability to prey on many species,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127">\n        <a href="#cite_note-127">\n         [123]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       the population of Burmese pythons exploded, with possibly as many as 300,000 in the Everglades alone.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Snow_et_al..2C_2007a_128-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Snow_et_al..2C_2007a-128">\n         [124]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Efforts have been made to curb the thriving population of these\n       <a href="/wiki/Invasive_species" title="Invasive species">\n        invasive\n       </a>\n       snakes, including a ban on importation of the species to the United States since January\xc2\xa02012 and increased regulations on ownership of a boa constrictor or python.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129">\n        <a href="#cite_note-129">\n         [125]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ferriter_et_al._2009_130-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Ferriter_et_al._2009-130">\n         [126]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Louisiana_2">\n        Louisiana\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Andrew&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Louisiana">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <p>\n       On August 26, George H. W. Bush toured devastated areas of Louisiana with\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Governor_of_Louisiana" title="Governor of Louisiana">\n        Governor\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Edwin_Edwards" title="Edwin Edwards">\n        Edwin Edwards\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131">\n        <a href="#cite_note-131">\n         [127]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       President Bush remarked, "The destruction from this storm goes beyond anything we have known in recent years," but noted that damage was less severe than in Florida. After his visit to Louisiana, President Bush declared only\n       <a href="/wiki/Terrebonne_Parish,_Louisiana" title="Terrebonne Parish, Louisiana">\n        Terrebonne Parish\n       </a>\n       as a disaster area,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-applebome_76-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-applebome-76">\n         [72]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       but later included\n       <a href="/wiki/List_of_parishes_in_Louisiana" title="List of parishes in Louisiana">\n        34 other parishes\n       </a>\n       under this declaration.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132">\n        <a href="#cite_note-132">\n         [128]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       FEMA initially opened five field offices throughout Louisiana. These centers allowed residents to submit applications for aid.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133">\n        <a href="#cite_note-133">\n         [129]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       After Franklin mayor Sam Jones and Congressman\n       <a href="/wiki/Billy_Tauzin" title="Billy Tauzin">\n        Billy Tauzin\n       </a>\n       criticized FEMA for failing to open a field office in Franklin, FEMA promised to do so. In the first few days following the storm,\n       <a href="/wiki/Louisiana_National_Guard" title="Louisiana National Guard">\n        Louisiana National Guard\n       </a>\n       members and local residents worked to remove debris such as downed trees, roofing shingles, and torn aluminum siding. The state National Guard also dispatched water purification units and tanks with filled potable water.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-salina_134-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-salina-134">\n         [130]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       About 1,300\xc2\xa0National Guardsmen were deployed to southern Louisiana.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sba_135-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-sba-135">\n         [131]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In early September, officials announced that 1,400\xc2\xa0mobile homes, homes, and apartments would become available to residents whose dwellings became uninhabitable.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sba_135-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-sba-135">\n         [131]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       House Resolution 5620 also included disaster aid to the state of Louisiana.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-os_90-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-os-90">\n         [86]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hr5620_91-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-hr5620-91">\n         [87]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In early December, the\n       <a href="/wiki/Small_Business_Administration" title="Small Business Administration">\n        Small Business Administration\n       </a>\n       (SBA) approved $33.2\xc2\xa0million worth of low-interest loans for repairs to homes and businesses. By then, FEMA had received about 43,600 applications for aid, while approving $35.9\xc2\xa0million in grants to over 18,000 households that were ineligible for loans from the SBA or were uninsured. In addition to the mobile homes already provided, FEMA spent $22.6 million on disaster housing.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136">\n        <a href="#cite_note-136">\n         [132]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <div style="clear:both;">\n      </div>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">\n        See also\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Andrew&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit style="display:table-row">\n         <span style="display:table-cell;padding:0.2em;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center">\n          <img alt="" class="noviewer" data-file-height="2004" cyclones portal\n          </a>\n         </span>\n        </li>\n       </ul>\n      </div>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/List_of_Florida_hurricanes_(1975%E2%80%9399)" title="List dollar">\n            USD\n           </a>\n           amounts of their respective year.\n          </span>\n         </li>\n         <li id="cite_note-52">\n          <span class="mw-cite-backlink">\n           <b>\n            <a href="#cite_ref-52">\n             ^\n            </a>\n           </b>\n          </span>\n          <span class="reference-text">\n           An indirect death is defined as a fatality that can be linked to the hurricane, but not caused by its direct effects. For example, several of the victims died of a heart attack induced by the storm.\n           <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51">\n            <a href="#cite_note-51">\n             [48]\n            </a>\n           </sup>\n          </span>\n         </li>\n        </ol>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="References">\n        References\n
